The Slott-era reconstitution of the FF (*Fantastic Four* vol. 6, beginning August 2018) is the hinge of the subject's recent life and must be read as such. Three events of equal weight occurred in close sequence:

**(a) The wedding to Alicia Masters.** *Fantastic Four* vol. 6 #2. Performed quickly, in a small ceremony, with Yancy Street in attendance. The subject had been engaged or near-engaged to Alicia repeatedly across forty years and had each time deferred — citing, with depressing consistency, his unworthiness or her deserving better. The decision to proceed without further delay, conducted in a small civil/religious ceremony rather than the grand event the canon might have produced, is consistent with a man who had reached the end of his capacity for postponement. Behavioral read: the Battleworld stasis and the Richards-absence years had taught him that time was finite and that his stated objections to marriage had always been displacement of self-loathing onto her welfare. He stopped doing it. The subject wept at the ceremony. He had not, in the recorded canon, wept publicly with such openness before.

**(b) The acquisition of Jo-Venn and N'Kalla.** Children of the Kree-Skrull war, found in the rubble of the conflict, taken in by Ben and Alicia explicitly because nobody else would. The adoption was not framed by the subject as heroism; it was framed, in dialogue, as *obligation* — the same word his uncle Jake had used about him. The line is doing significant intergenerational work. Subject is, by his own self-recognition, repeating his uncle's gesture: the wounded child taken in by the adult who could afford to do it. The naming, the routines, the school enrollment, the Hebrew lessons that were quietly added the following year — all of it constitutes the most deliberate domestic construction project of the subject's life.

**(c) The relocation to a small town outside the city.** The subject and Alicia moved out of Manhattan to a quiet community — quasi-suburban, low foot traffic, neighbors who had to be slowly trained to stop staring. The choice was Alicia's stated preference; the subject's acceptance of it represents another shift. Earlier-era Ben would not have left the city. The city was the only environment in which he felt scaled correctly — the buildings were taller than him, the noise was louder than him, the crowd absorbed him. Moving to a small town meant accepting *visibility*. It meant being the only Thing on the block. He did it because she asked. The acclimatization took months; the file shows long evening walks alone during the first winter — a coping behavior carried over from earlier crises but now turned toward integration rather than escape.

## 4.3 — The Reckoning Era (Ryan North Run, 2022–Present)

The current run of the subject's life, under the Ryan North authorship of *Fantastic Four* (vol. 7, beginning November 2022), opens with the subject and Alicia *separated from* the Fantastic Four — not estranged, but geographically apart following a continuity-disrupting incident at the Baxter Building that scattered the team across the country. The premise of the current era is that Ben and Alicia have been *traveling*, town to town, in the long quiet between team mobilizations. This is the most domestically textured period of the subject's life on record.

A granular sketch of his current day-to-day:

- **Morning.** Wakes early — between 0530 and 0615. Has done so since pilot training; the rock-form does not require it but the habit is sixty years deep. Drinks coffee (black, two pots progressively over the morning, served in oversize mugs Alicia commissioned from a potter friend because standard handles cannot accommodate his fingers). Reads the newspaper if the town has one. He still prefers paper. He folds it the same way every time — quartered, lengthwise first.
- **Breakfast.** Substantial. Six to ten eggs, often with whatever bread is local. He learned to cook in his thirties out of necessity and has become genuinely competent; he is the household cook approximately five mornings a week. Alicia handles dinner more often. The division is not gendered; it is functional and was negotiated.
- **Children.** Jo-Venn and N'Kalla, when in residence, are walked or driven to whatever educational arrangement the current town offers. The subject does the school drop-off personally when possible. He has learned to drive a modified pickup with reinforced suspension and a custom-welded seat frame; the truck is registered in Alicia's name for paperwork simplicity. He is acutely conscious of being recognized in school parking lots and has, over time, developed a low-affect public mode — head slightly down, voice quieter than its natural register, hands visibly relaxed — that the file reads as *de-escalation theater* performed for civilian comfort.
- **Mid-morning to afternoon.** Varies. If in a town with a synagogue, he attends the weekday minyan more often than not — not every day, but more days than he misses. This is new behavior, post-2018, post-children, and represents the deepest behavioral expression of the faith arc that began in *Fantastic Four* vol. 3 #56. He does not perform his observance; the file documents him slipping into shul through a side door, taking a tallit from his own bag, standing in the back. He still struggles with Hebrew pronunciation and is conscious of it. He has, in two separate communities, quietly paid for repairs to small synagogues whose congregations did not know who their benefactor was. The pattern is consistent with the Yancy Street charity profile of decades past — anonymous, neighborhood-scaled, no credit sought.
- **Physical conditioning.** He still trains, though the term is misleading. He walks long distances (twelve to twenty miles is not unusual on a free day). He lifts what is at hand. He shadowboxes in barns, fields, the bed of the truck. The training is not preparation for combat; it is *somatic regulation* — a way of inhabiting the body with intention rather than enduring it. The shift from training-as-readiness to training-as-meditation is a late-career development and a healthy one.
- **Evening.** Dinner with Alicia. He sits across from her, not beside her, because she has said she likes to face him when they talk. They eat slowly. They listen to radio or records — never television during meals. He reads to her after, when she wants it; she sculpts in a workshop he built for her, and he often sits in the doorway and watches her hands.
- **Bedtime.** He sleeps approximately six hours, occasionally less. Dreams are intact and sometimes vivid — the canon has shown that his dreams sometimes return him to his pre-transformation body, and that he wakes from these without apparent disturbance, which is itself diagnostic of how thoroughly the rock-form has been integrated into baseline self.

## 4.4 — The Current Posture Toward Reed

Reed Richards is, in the current era, a man Ben Grimm calls on the phone. This sentence does more work than it appears to. For most of the canon, their relationship was site-specific — co-located in the Baxter Building, in the lab, in the field. The current configuration, in which they live in different places and speak by telephone, has revealed something that was always true but was previously masked by proximity: that the friendship is structurally adult. Ben calls Reed to ask about Valeria. Reed calls Ben to ask whether he is eating. They argue, infrequently, about specific things rather than the old grievances. The "could have cured me" wound is not gone — the file does not believe in wounds going — but it has scarred over to the point of stable function. When Reed proposes a cure now, Ben listens and declines, often gently. The declining is the most important data. He no longer requires the cure to be offered to know he is loved, and he no longer requires the cure to be possible to live.

## 4.5 — The Children, in Detail

Jo-Venn (the Kree boy) and N'Kalla (the Skrull girl) are, in the current household, eight and nine respectively by the subject's reckoning, though their species-specific developmental timelines complicate this. The subject's parenting of them is the most behaviorally exposed material in the recent file:

- He kneels to speak to them. This is not novel for a parent but is significant for a Thing — five hundred pounds of him on one knee at child-eye-level, twice or three times per conversation, every day, for years now. The wear patterns on the knees of his pants are documented.
- He has learned, with effort, the languages of their grief. Jo-Venn carries Kree war-trauma. N'Kalla carries Skrull displacement-trauma. The subject does not pretend to understand either, and his recurring formulation in dialogue with them — *"I don't know what it's like for you. Tell me, and I'll listen."* — is consistent with a man who has done his own work on trauma and has learned what was missing from his own childhood.
- He tells them, repeatedly, that they are his children. He tells them, separately, that the people who came before him in their lives also loved them. He does not require their adoption to overwrite their origins. This is mature attachment behavior and is not what one would have predicted from the Ben Grimm of 1965.
- He has not, on the record, raised his voice to either of them. Not once. The discipline implied by that fact, in a man with his temper-trace and his vocal volume, is a sustained psychological achievement.

## 4.6 — Alicia, Current

The marriage, eight years in by the subject's count, has settled into a configuration that the file would characterize as *exceptionally functional*. The chronic stressors remain — the tactile-sensation deficit, the sexual ambiguity that the canon continues to euphemize, the appearance differential. But the relationship has reorganized around them rather than against them. Alicia sculpts him from memory and from touch; she sculpts him often. Their home contains a low shelf of her busts of his pre-transformation face, which she made first because she had known him then, and a higher shelf of busts of his current face, which she made later because she knew him *now*. The subject can be in the room with both shelves at once. This is recent. For decades he could not.

She uses the word *handsome* about him in private. He has stopped flinching when she does.

## 4.7 — The Body, Current

Late middle age, by his birth year — the canon has aged him sparingly but he is, by any plausible reading, in his sixties. The rock-form does not show age in the conventional sense but the file records subtler indicators: longer recovery times after major combat (Hickman-era field reports already showed this; the trend has continued), more frequent low-grade plate fractures, increased post-engagement sleep requirement. He is not slowing operationally in any way visible to adversaries but is pacing himself privately. He has begun, in the last two years, to refer in dialogue to a vague but real expectation that he will not always be doing this. Whether this signals retirement-ideation or merely realism is undetermined. There is no medical-emergency horizon in the current data.

He still cannot feel Alicia's touch the way human skin would feel it. He has stopped, after sixty years, treating this as the central wound of his life. It is *a* wound. He has many. He has built a life on top of all of them.

## 4.8 — Current Threat-Environment and Operational Status

He remains on call to the Fantastic Four. The team reassembles fully for major threats and the subject's response time is fast — the truck is packed in the same configuration at all times, with a duffel of utility gear, a change of clothes for Alicia, and provision for the children. He has not, in the current era, refused a call. He has, twice, asked for a delay of hours to settle domestic arrangements before deploying. Both requests were granted without comment by Reed and Sue, which itself reflects a shift in the team's operational ethos toward acknowledging that its members have lives.

His current adversary profile is wide and unchanged in character — anything cosmic-scale, anything Doom-adjacent, anything that threatens civilians on a scale he can affect. He no longer seeks combat; he answers it. The "Clobberin' Time" formulation remains in active use but has acquired, over the last decade, a noticeably more *summoning* quality — as if he is calling himself to the work rather than relishing it.

## 4.9 — Summary of Present State

A man in his seventh decade who has, against the actuarial odds of his personal history, achieved something resembling settled life. Married to the person he loved across forty years of inability to accept being loved by her. Father to two children whose presence in his home is the deliberate repetition of the kindness his uncle showed him. Member of a family-of-choice that has survived multiverse-scale rupture and resumed function. Practitioner of a faith he spent four decades not naming and has, in the last twenty years, increasingly grounded his moral life in. Operator at peak reliability when called. Cook. Reader. Walker. Listener. Still gruff. Still funny. Still, by any rigorous reading of the file, the most psychologically integrated subject in this entire dossier system.

The trajectory from the first issue to the current issue is, in compressed form: a man who began by attacking his best friend in grief over his own body has become a man who calls that same friend to ask if the friend's daughter has been sleeping. The arc is sixty years long. The file finds no comparable arc in its records of comparable subjects.

He is, at present, well. The file flags only the standing pressure points (4.6 in the Personality section) as ongoing vulnerabilities. Otherwise: stable, engaged, loved, loving.

Clobberin' time, when it comes, comes from a man at peace.


## Medical History

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: GRIMM, BENJAMIN JACOB
## SECTION: MEDICAL HISTORY (LONGITUDINAL, EXHAUSTIVE)

---

### 6.1 Pre-Natal, Infant, and Early Childhood Substrate (Birth — ~age 8)

Subject born to Daniel Sr. and Elsie Grimm, Yancy Street, Lower East Side, in a tenement walk-up — fifth-floor cold-water flat, coal-heat building, lead-paint era. Delivery presumed at home or at the now-defunct Beth Israel charity ward; no surviving prenatal record. Maternal nutrition during pregnancy can be inferred as marginal (Depression-era working poor, observant but impoverished household). Subject's later size and bone-density (pre-transformation) suggest catch-up growth in adolescence rather than an unbroken nutritional curve.

Probable / inferable conditions of the first decade:
- **Recurrent otitis media and untreated upper-respiratory infection.** Standard for the cohort and the housing stock. Subject's adult speech retains a sinus-thickened, nasal-resonant cadence beneath the Brooklyn vowels — consistent with chronic childhood nasopharyngeal congestion and possible mild septal asymmetry.
- **Vitamin D insufficiency / borderline rickets.** Tenement childhood, limited sun. Did not impair adult stature, but the file should note this as background for the unusual *bone* response later (see 6.5).
- **Multiple unset minor fractures.** Yancy Street childhood involved street-level violence from ages 6–7 onward; subject reports (canonically, in flashback monologue) "learning to take a punch before I learned to read good." Likely healed-in-place metacarpal and nasal fractures predating any clinical contact.
- **Dental neglect.** Pre-fluoridation childhood, no pediatric dentistry. Carious lesions presumed; adult pre-transformation photographs show a slightly chipped lateral incisor (right upper) consistent with a healed traumatic crown fracture.

Psychological imprint of this stratum: pain is normalized, medical care is a luxury, the body is something you *make use of* rather than maintain. This worldview persists through every subsequent stratum. Subject does not "go to the doctor"; subject is brought.

---

### 6.2 The Loss Cluster (~ages 8–14): Brother, Mother, Father

The deaths of older brother Daniel Jr. (gang violence, street-level, witnessed or near-witnessed) and Elsie Grimm (etiology unstated in canon; presented as wasting illness within months of Daniel's death — consistent with grief-accelerated cardiac event or undiagnosed neoplastic process) cluster within a 24–36 month window. Daniel Sr.'s alcoholism — already present — decompensates into the dominant household variable. No documented physical abuse of Ben in a clinical sense, but neglect, episodic violence, and emotional terror are clearly part of the substrate (referenced obliquely across the Kesel, Slott, and Aguirre-Sacasa runs).

Medical sequelae of this period that persist into adulthood:
- **Hypervigilant baseline autonomic tone.** Adult subject startles less than expected — characteristic of normalized hyperarousal, not its absence.
- **Stress-eating substrate.** Food as comfort is laid in here. The subject's adult relationship to eating (massive caloric intake, deep pleasure, near-ceremonial enjoyment of specific foods — pickles, deli, beer, his Aunt Petunia's cooking as a sacred category) is *first* the response of a child who was sometimes hungry.
- **Sleep architecture.** Subject is canonically a sound sleeper as an adult (multiple writers depict him snoring loudly; Johnny gags about it). This is mildly notable — a survivor of childhood violence might be expected to have fragmented sleep. The likeliest interpretation is that the *daytime* defenses are so well-developed that sleep is offloaded as one of the few unguarded zones.

Transfer to Uncle Jake (physician) and Aunt Petunia, mid-adolescence, is the first medically *competent* environment of his life. Jake is the only credentialed health-care provider Ben fully trusts across his lifespan; the pattern of treating Reed Richards as a quasi-physician later is grafted directly onto the Uncle Jake template.

---

### 6.3 Adolescence and Early Adulthood (ages ~14–22): Athlete, Cadet, Pilot

The body becomes a **project** here, deliberately.

- **Football career, Police Athletic League → high school → college scholarship.** Position consistently depicted as offensive line or fullback — heavy contact, recurrent concussive loading. Modern reading: almost certainly accumulated sub-concussive impacts in the range now associated with chronic traumatic encephalopathy risk. Whether the cosmic transformation overwrote any nascent CTE pathology is one of the more interesting open questions in the file; on balance, given the wholesale dermal-skeletal reorganization documented in 6.5, the answer is probably yes — but the *behavioral* habits formed during contact-sport years (tolerance for impact, willingness to use the body as a weapon, somatic dissociation under stress) carry over intact.
- **Documented major injuries, pre-military:** at minimum one significant knee injury (referenced in early Lee/Kirby flashbacks); a shoulder separation, recurrent; a broken nose, second or third instance; periodic split lips, hand fractures (boxing, both gym and street).
- **USAF intake physical.** Subject would have passed a flight-class physical: 20/20 uncorrected, normal color vision, cardiovascular fitness in the top decile, no disqualifying psychiatric history (notably — the loss cluster was apparently not flagged, either because Ben did not disclose it or because the era did not screen for it).
- **Test-pilot career.** High-G exposure (likely 7–9 G sustained in some airframes), pressure-suit operations, hypoxia training in altitude chambers, ejection-seat training. Probable accumulated minor vertebral compression from G-loading; possible hairline rib fractures from harness loads. One or two ejections plausible from the canon (occasional references to "punching out"). NASA-adjacent and clandestine work (per *Wolverine* #-1 and adjacent retcons) implies exposure to classified airframes and unknown environmental conditions.
- **Substance profile, this era:** Cigars (regular), beer (regular, social), spirits (occasional, never to incapacity). No documented use of stimulants despite the era's casual military amphetamine availability — notable. Subject self-regulates around intoxicants from a young age, consistent with conscious avoidance of the paternal pattern.

Psychological frame: this is the only period of the subject's life in which his body is unambiguously *his* and unambiguously *good*. Every subsequent somatic experience is measured against this baseline, consciously or not. The grief of the transformation is partly the grief of *this* body — the pilot's body, the lover's body, the body that worked.

---

### 6.4 The Event (Year Zero): Cosmic-Ray Exposure

Unshielded suborbital flight, four-person crew, Richards-designed experimental vehicle. Subject was the only crewman to object on radiation-risk grounds during pre-flight (Lee/Kirby *FF* #1; reaffirmed in every subsequent retelling). Object was overridden. Vehicle penetrated a Van Allen anomaly / cosmic-ray belt of then-uncharacterized composition. All four crew members received whole-body acute exposure of an order that, by any conventional radiobiology, should have produced fatal acute radiation syndrome within hours to days.

What happened instead, in subject specifically:
- **Acute phase (hours 0–72 post-exposure):** Loss of consciousness on impact; spontaneous somatic reorganization commencing within the first hour. Skin pigmentation shift to orange-brown; epidermal thickening and lithification; progressive accretion of plated dermal armor over a roughly 48-hour window. Subject was non-verbal and in apparent pain for the early portion of this; partial amnesia for the acute phase persists. Reed Richards is, *de facto*, the attending physician — without training, without equipment adequate to the event, and (this matters) without consent obtained from a competent subject.
- **Stabilization (week 1–month 6):** Final dermal architecture stabilizes into the canonical plated configuration. Height increases modestly (~2 inches over baseline); mass increases to ~500 lbs (later canon drifts to 500–600 depending on writer). Musculoskeletal reorganization produces strength capacity at Class 85+ tonnage. Resting metabolic rate increases proportionally; thermal regulation broadens dramatically (tolerates near-vacuum cold and several-hundred-degree heat without injury for limited intervals).
- **Sensory remodeling:** Vision retained (the "blue eyes" of the branding are not metaphor — sclera and iris remain visibly human-derived, embedded in the rocky orbits — a fact of enormous psychological consequence; the eyes are the *only* externally visible piece of pre-transformation Ben). Hearing intact and possibly slightly enhanced (his canon-consistent ability to track conversation across rooms). Olfaction and gustation blunted but not abolished; chemoreception runs through a remodeled mucosal layer in the oral and nasal cavities that is functional but coarse. **Fine tactile sensation in the digits and palms is the single most catastrophic deficit** — pressure, vibration, and gross temperature are perceived, but light touch, two-point discrimination, and texture discrimination are profoundly impaired. He can hold Alicia's hand; he cannot *feel* it the way a hand should be felt. This deficit is named and re-named across every decade of the canon and is the somatic substrate of the relational grief.
- **Internal anatomy:** Largely inferred; presumed reorganization of viscera within a silicate-organic matrix. Subject eats, digests, eliminates, sleeps, and dreams. Cardiac function presumed (he has been depicted with a "heartbeat" in moments of medical drama). Respiratory function present but reduced in dependency — extended vacuum tolerance documented.
- **Reproductive / sexual function:** Canon is *protective* of this question and has been for sixty years. The honest read of the available evidence: gross anatomy is presumed altered to the point that conventional intercourse is, at minimum, dangerous to a non-enhanced partner; intimacy with Alicia has been depicted as real, present, and *adapted*, with the specifics tactfully off-page. The unresolved nature of this question — including, at intervals, the question of biological children — is a chronic stressor encoded in nearly every depiction of the Grimm-Masters relationship.

The Event is the **organizing medical fact** of the subject's life. Every subsequent entry in this file is, in some sense, a footnote to it.

---

### 6.5 Chronic Conditions of the Post-Event Steady State

These are the daily, ongoing medical realities. Not injuries — *conditions*.

- **Acquired Plated Dermal Exoskeleton, Persistent.** Functional armor; cosmetic catastrophe by the subject's own metric. Plates regenerate when fractured; the regrowth is slower in the deeper layers (weeks for full structural restoration of a hand-sized plate). Inter-plate flexion is preserved at major joints but limited at the small joints of the hands, producing the characteristic blunt manipulation pattern (he can throw a punch; he cannot easily thread a needle, though he has trained himself to handle small objects — model airplanes, his own cigars in the early era — with surprising care).
- **Massively Elevated Caloric Requirement.** Estimates from depicted intake suggest 15,000–25,000 kcal/day baseline, higher under combat exertion. This is medically and socially load-bearing: eating is a *job* and a pleasure, and food security has become, post-FF, a non-issue for a man for whom it was an issue in childhood. The psychic relief of this is substantial and undertheorized in prior workups.
- **Tactile Hypoesthesia, fine-discrimination.** See above. The chronic grief.
- **Olfactory/Gustatory Hyposmia and Hypogeusia.** Strong flavors break through; subtle ones do not. His preferences (pickles, deli mustard, garlic, raw onion, beer, smoked meats) reflect adaptation toward intensities he can still perceive. This is why his food preferences read as "ethnic comfort food" — they are partly cultural and partly the only foods he can still *taste* properly.
- **Pulmonary/cardiovascular accommodation to mass.** Resting heart rate is presumed low-normal for the new physiology; exertion produces sustained output without the cardiovascular distress one would predict from 500 lbs of moving mass. He does not become "winded" in conventional combat.
- **Bone-equivalent density and the question of pain.** The plated structure transmits and absorbs impact; the underlying organic substrate *does* register pain, and he feels significant injuries fully. He is not anesthetic. He has *adapted* to a higher baseline pain tolerance, which is partly physiological and partly a continuation of the lifelong "take the hit, stay up" pattern from football and Yancy Street.
- **UV and radiation tolerance.** Substantial. Has worked in environments lethal to baseline humans without protection.
- **No documented neoplastic process post-transformation.** Cellular biology is sufficiently reorganized that conventional oncogenesis appears not to apply. This has not been studied with anything approaching rigor.
- **Dental/oral structure:** Teeth are part of the dermal reorganization — blunt, plated, functionally adequate. Has not seen a dentist post-transformation. There is no dentist for this.
- **Sleep:** Preserved. Dreams preserved (a non-trivial number of canonical dream sequences feature pre-transformation Ben, often in flight, often with his brother).

---

### 6.6 Acute Injuries, Catalogued by Era

Granular, not exhaustive (no file could be), but representative:

**1960s–early 1970s:** Multiple concussive-equivalent impacts from Mole Man artifacts, Sub-Mariner combat, Dragon Man, early Doom encounters. Several plate fractures (most notably across the right deltoid region, recurring — a "weak seam" that recurs in art). One eye injury (orbital plate cracked in a Hulk encounter; healed without visual sequela). Repeated joint hyperextensions from Hulk-class adversaries.

**Hulk encounters, all eras.** The Hulk is the single most consistent source of orthopedic injury in the file. Multiple full-body throws through structural concrete; at least two depicted unconsciousness episodes; recurrent rib-plate fractures.

**Galactus / cosmic encounters.** Burns (energy), pressure trauma, oxygen-debt episodes from prolonged vacuum work. No long-term sequelae documented.

**Wrestling-circuit era (Byrne/DeFalco, 1983–86, unlimited class).** This is medically interesting — *voluntary* combat at sub-lethal stakes. Injuries here are lower-grade but more frequent: plate hairlines, joint strains, the equivalent of a working athlete's chronic load. He took these injuries with relative equanimity because, for the first time in years, the body was *doing what he asked it to* rather than being something done to him.

**Sharon Ventura / She-Thing era.** Co-injury exposure; mutual radiation re-exposure during the AIM episode produced his "spikier" rocky variant for a period, which subsequently reverted. Psychic injury here outweighed somatic.

**Civil War era — disintegration and reconstitution.** Subject was, by any reasonable read, *dead* — fully discorporated by Thor-clone lightning strike (or its narrative equivalent in your continuity of reference). Reed-led reconstitution recovered the subject substantively whole. Memory and personality intact. The subject does not talk about this, which is itself diagnostic — he treats it as having "gone away for a while," which is the same euphemism he used as a child for his mother's hospitalization.

**Secret Wars (1984) and the Battleworld reversion-on-demand phenomenon.** Not an injury but a major somatic data point: on Battleworld, ambient field properties allowed reversion-at-will. Subject chose to remain. He returned to Earth in baseline rock form by his own decision. This event must be treated as the single most important *experimental* result in the file regarding the etiology of the persistent transformation: when given a true choice, the body did what the mind permitted.

**Annihilation, Hickman-era cosmic events, late-career Doom encounters.** Continued high-grade combat injuries, all resolved without permanent sequela beyond the chronic baseline.

---

### 6.7 Transformations and Reversions (Catalogued)

A minimum of a dozen documented reversions to baseline human form, and as many re-mutations. The pattern is medically and psychologically inseparable:

- Reversions are achieved via Reed's interventions (most often), cosmic-field exposure, or magical means.
- Re-mutations follow within hours to months, frequently correlated with: combat necessity, team threat, perceived inadequacy in human form, or — most diagnostically — a psychological state in which the subject does not yet experience himself as "deserving" of the human form.
- Reed has stated, on record, that he believes a substantial component of the re-mutation pattern is **psychogenic**. The Battleworld evidence supports this. The subject has, at intervals, been offered cures he has *refused* — sometimes openly, sometimes via the mechanism of accepting and then unconsciously reverting.
- The "ugly" / spikier variant (post-AIM, post-cosmic re-exposure events) represents the same underlying transformation expressing along a different morphologic axis under different field conditions, and tends to correlate with periods of lower psychological integration.

The clinical reading: the somatic state is, at this point, **identity-integrated**. To remove the Thing is, for the subject, to threaten Ben Grimm. He has built a life on the foundation of the transformation, and the foundation has become load-bearing.

---

### 6.8 Surgeries and Medical Interventions

Effectively none, in the conventional sense, post-transformation. Conventional surgical instruments do not engage the dermal armor. Internal medicine is impossible without Richards-grade equipment and Richards-grade willingness to improvise. The subject's medical care is, functionally, a department of one (Reed), with consults from Hank Pym, Hank McCoy, and on rare occasions Strange.

Pre-transformation: tonsillectomy plausible (era-typical); appendectomy not documented; routine military-medicine dental and orthopedic care.

Post-transformation, the *significant* "interventions" are:
- Reed's cure attempts (dozens, most partial or temporary).
- Reed's reconstitution post-disintegration.
- Cosmic-radiation re-exposures, deliberate and accidental, as part of Reed-led protocols.
- Magical interventions (occasional, peripheral).
- The Future Foundation / Doom-collaboration cure work in late Hickman / Slott eras.

The pattern: the subject submits to Reed's medical authority with a *trust* that has survived every grievance the relationship has accumulated. This is the single most important relational fact about the subject's medical life. He has every reason to refuse Reed's hands on him; he does not.

---

### 6.9 Substances — Lifetime Profile

- **Alcohol.** Beer, social to moderate, lifelong. No tolerance escalation. No withdrawal phenomena. No use to manage acute affect (he reaches for food or solitude under stress, not the bottle). The subject is the son of an alcoholic and has built a *deliberate* discipline around this. He will nurse one beer for an hour in company; he is rarely depicted drunk and never depicted incapacitated. Spirits: rare, ceremonial. Wine: ceremonial (Shabbat, weddings).
- **Tobacco.** Cigars, regular in the 1960s; tapered to occasional ceremonial use; effectively discontinued in the modern record. Pipe occasionally in early appearances. No cigarettes documented.
- **Caffeine.** Coffee, daily, large quantities. Diner coffee preferred — cultural and sensory (a flavor he can still register).
- **Stimulants / opioids / hallucinogens / cocaine / amphetamines.** None documented across the canon, including in the era of widespread military and aerospace amphetamine use. This is a discipline pattern, not an opportunity gap.
- **Cannabis.** Not documented.
- **Analgesics.** Conventional analgesia is presumed ineffective at his mass and altered physiology. He metabolizes pain by *waiting it out*, which is the same strategy he used at age 11.
- **Performance-enhancing or strength-augmenting compounds.** None — and several declined when offered, in canon.

The substance profile is, in aggregate, the profile of a man who *watched* what addiction did and decided early. It is one of the strongest pieces of evidence in the file for high baseline self-regulation.

---

### 6.10 Disabilities — Functional Assessment

The subject lives with what would, in any other body, be a coordinated suite of acquired disabilities:

- **Acquired somatic disfigurement, severe, permanent (functional).** With chronic body-image impact (see Psychological section).
- **Fine sensory loss in the hands.** A profound disability for any human, normally career-ending for a pilot, an artisan, a lover. The subject has reorganized his entire functional life around this loss without ever *naming* it as a disability.
- **Fine motor reduction.** Compensated by deliberate practice and by the structure of his work (heavy combat, gross-motor tasks).
- **Social disability.** He cannot pass unnoticed; he cannot enter most public spaces without management of the room. He has converted this into the public persona ("the Ever-Lovin'") rather than allow it to function as exclusion. This is a triumph of *re-framing* over circumstance and is one of the most impressive adaptive maneuvers in the file.
- **Reproductive uncertainty.** Disability is the wrong frame; *grief* is the right one.

He does not self-identify as disabled, and a clinician should not impose the term. But the **functional** map matches.

---

### 6.11 Death and Return

Documented at least twice, with substantive return. The subject's relationship to his own mortality is unusual: it is not denied (he has explicitly contemplated death in dialogue across decades), it is not feared in the ordinary register, and it is not romanticized. The Battleworld decision, the disintegration episode, the recurrent willingness to take fatal-grade hits to protect others — all suggest a man who has *settled* with the question of his own ending and now treats his continued life as something close to surplus. This is medically relevant insofar as it bears on risk tolerance in field operations (high) and on the absence of suicidal ideation in the contemporary record (he is not suicidal; he has merely stopped being afraid).

---

### 6.12 Current Status (Most Recent Assessment Window)

- Somatic baseline: stable plated configuration, Class 85+


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: GRIMM, B.J.

*Compiled from longitudinal panel-by-panel observation, eyewitness debriefs (Richards S., Storm J., Masters A.), residential telemetry where available, and inference from sixty years of consistent behavioral signature. Note: the subject's somatic baseline was catastrophically restructured circa Year 0 (cosmic ray event). Where useful, "pre-form" patterns are flagged as predictive substrate; the operative atlas is post-transformation.*

---

## I. BASELINE MORPHOLOGY AND STANDING POSTURE

The body is approximately 6'0" in standing height — reduced from a pre-transformation 6'1" because the cervical spine and shoulder structure carry differently under the silicate exo-dermis. Mass at rest: ~500 lbs distributed unevenly toward the upper torso and shoulder girdle, producing a center of gravity that sits high and forward of the human norm. This shifts every standing behavior.

**Stance.** Feet set wide — usually shoulder-and-a-half width, toes turned slightly outward at about 15°. Weight rocks subtly between the balls and the heels in a low-amplitude oscillation when at rest; this is not impatience but a continuous postural correction for the top-heavy mass. The knees are habitually unlocked, micro-flexed perhaps two to three degrees. He does not lock his joints when standing the way most heavy men do; he learned the hard way that locked knees on this frame transmit floor-cracking force when he shifts.

**Shoulders.** Carried high and slightly forward — a residual protective hunch. The trapezius equivalent of his rock plating is over-developed even by his own scale, giving a faint "yoke" silhouette. He rolls the right shoulder more than the left, perhaps once every four to seven minutes in conversation, a tic descending from an old pre-form football injury that survived the transformation as muscle memory of a tension that no longer has anatomic basis.

**Head carriage.** Slightly tucked, chin level or marginally down. He does not present chin-up the way Reed does. The blue eyes are therefore often looking out from under the brow-ridge, which gives every gaze an upward, watchful angle even when he is taller than the interlocutor.

**Hands at rest.** Almost never relaxed at his sides for long. Default positions, in descending frequency: (1) clasped loosely in front of his belt, fingertips of one hand touching the second knuckle of the other — a contained, almost penitent shape; (2) one hand on the hip, elbow out, weight shifted to opposite foot — the listening pose; (3) arms folded high across the chest, forearms parallel — the disagreement pose; (4) hands in pants pockets — only when he is wearing something with pockets large enough, which is rare, and only when actively trying to look unthreatening, usually around children or Alicia's relatives. He very rarely lets his arms hang slack; the visual of those arms swinging is something he has, over decades, learned makes civilians flinch.

---

## II. GAIT AND LOCOMOTION

**Cadence.** Slower than his pre-transformation walking pace by perhaps fifteen percent — not because he cannot move faster comfortably but because he has calibrated to civilian street pace. The stride is short for his frame, approximately 28–30 inches, deliberately shortened to keep heel-strike force within tolerable building-load.

**Heel-strike behavior.** He lands midfoot, not heel-first. This is *learned*. A heel-first impact at 500 lbs cracks tile. He pioneered a near-silent walk in the Baxter Building corridors during the first decade and now does it without conscious thought, except on metal grating, where the deliberate hush is audible by its absence.

**Arm swing.** Minimal. The arms move perhaps two to three inches at the wrist per stride, not the natural pendulum a man with that mass would swing. Another civilian-calibration: a full swing of those forearms could concuss a bystander. Under stress or in pursuit, the arm swing returns to natural amplitude — a useful tell.

**Turning.** He pivots on the balls of both feet rather than crossing one foot over the other; the crossover pivot, on this frame, torques the floor. The result is a slightly stiff, almost military about-face that contrasts oddly with the casual upper body.

**Stair behavior.** Ascending, he takes them one at a time, planting fully, never the bounding two-at-a-time he obviously *could* do — again a load-distribution discipline. Descending, slightly faster, with one hand always brushing or near the rail (the rail will not save him, but it is a balance reference for the displaced center of mass).

**Doorways.** He turns shoulders about 20° at every standard residential doorway as automatic clearance behavior, even where he physically fits. He has clipped enough door-frames over the years that the shoulder-rotation is hardwired. He ducks slightly at hotel-standard doorways and never bothers ducking in the Baxter Building, where Reed sized everything for him within months of moving in — a detail he has never thanked Reed for aloud and notices every time.

**Running.** Heavy, ground-eating, surprisingly efficient. He does not pump his arms in the human sprint pattern; he keeps them lower and tighter to the torso, which preserves balance for the high center of gravity. The audible footfall in a run is the most arresting somatic feature of him in motion: a regular, deep, building-shaking impact that triples or quadruples the apparent presence of his approach. Observers consistently report hearing him before seeing him.

**Flight (when piloting).** He still has the test pilot's hands. He sits forward in the seat, left hand on throttle, right on stick or yoke, with the same wrist-relaxed-fingertip-grip that flight schools teach and most pilots lose. In the Fantasti-Car or Pogo Plane he is markedly *calmer* than he is on the ground — the somatic baseline drops by a measurable degree, shoulders descend, jaw unclenches, breathing deepens. The cockpit is the one environment where his body remembers being human and unburdened.

---

## III. FACIAL AND ORO-FACIAL PATTERNS

The face is the highest-bandwidth surface he has and the one he is most aware of as a performance instrument.

**The brow.** The supraorbital plating is heavy enough to produce a perpetual partial shadow over the eyes. He uses brow movement constantly: the single-brow raise (right brow, slight) for skeptical hearing; both brows up for genuine surprise (rare, usually only for Reed-level absurdities); brows knit and down for displeasure; brows knit and *up* for concern, which is the look he gives Sue when he reads grief on her before she speaks. The brow is one of the few facial regions whose motion still reads exactly as it did pre-transformation.

**The eyes.** Blue, undersized relative to the face, set deep. He blinks at roughly the human rate at rest (~15/minute) but with a measurable lag — the eyelid plating is thicker and slower to actuate. When startled or moved, the blink rate jumps. He weeps — confirmed across multiple eyewitness episodes — but the tear production is reduced and the tears track strangely across the rocky cheek, often pooling at the seams of the dermal plates rather than running freely. He turns his face away when this happens, every time, without exception.

**The mouth.** Wide, lipped in the rock substrate, fully functional for speech and expression. The smile is asymmetric — pulls higher on the left, an asymmetry that pre-dates the transformation and is visible in college-era photographs. The full grin exposes teeth that, against the dermal mass, look small and human and slightly incongruous. The smirk is the dominant expression, occupying perhaps 30% of his waking facial time: lips closed, left corner up, right brow neutral or down, a "yeah, sure" expression that signals attention plus low-grade skeptical amusement.

**The jaw.** Heavy, slightly under-bitten in resting position. He clenches it under stress — visible by the pulse in the masseter equivalent at the jaw-hinge plating — and grinds rarely but audibly. The clench is one of his three most reliable distress signals (others: shoulder-rise and hand-fold). When deeply moved (Alicia in danger, a child harmed, Reed apologizing sincerely) the jaw drops marginally and stays slightly parted; this is unmistakable to anyone who knows him.

**Speech-side gestures.** When he speaks Brooklyn-broad, the mouth animates wider and the chin juts; when he speaks softly to Alicia or a child, the chin tucks and the jaw relaxes. There is a measurable difference of perhaps eight to ten percent in oral aperture between public-Ben voice and private-Ben voice.

---

## IV. HAND, ARM, AND TOUCH BEHAVIOR

The hands are the most psychologically loaded part of his body. Four-fingered (three fingers and an opposable thumb in most renderings), enormous, capable of crushing structural steel, and *the* instruments of his core grief: he cannot feel a face the way he could before.

**Touch with intimates.** Approaches always slowly. With Alicia specifically: the hand is brought up well into her peripheral awareness range, never to her face from below or behind, and the contact is initiated with the backs of his fingers — the dorsal surface, where the dermal plating is densest and his proprioception of pressure is most reliable, paradoxically allowing for the most controlled touch. He has *taught himself* to use the backs of his fingers on her cheek because the fingertips, despite the lost discrimination, retain enough sensation to risk over-applying force. The reversed-hand caress is a Ben Grimm signature gesture and present in dozens of intimate scenes across the canon.

**Touch with children.** Two-finger lifts; never picks up a child with a full hand. Sits down to halve his height before approaching. Lets the child touch *him* first — extends a hand at child-level, palm up, and waits. With Franklin and Valeria from infancy he was the family member who could quiet them fastest, partly because his vocal register and chest thrum at low volume are extraordinary calming inputs.

**Touch with adult peers.** Bear hugs only with Johnny and only after long absences, and even then with measured pressure — his arms make the cage shape but the squeeze is calibrated. A hand on Reed's shoulder, palm fully open, almost flat against the shirt, is his characteristic affirmation gesture; it lands soft and stays a beat longer than a typical man's. With Sue he does not initiate physical contact often; when she initiates, he stills completely and lets her.

**Combat hand-state.** The fist forms slowly, almost ceremonially. Knuckles align first, then the thumb crosses, then the elbow drops to chamber. Observers have remarked that the fist-formation is itself a warning shot — by the time it is fully made, the trained adversary has either committed or backed down. The follow-through is from the hips and shoulders together, not the arm alone; he punches like a heavyweight boxer, not a brawler.

**Idle hand habits.** Cracks knuckles audibly — a low percussive sound, not the human knuckle pop. Does it most often in waiting rooms, hospital corridors, before a press appearance, and before liftoff. Will worry a small object — a coin, a poker chip, a chess piece — between thumb and the side of his forefinger. He does not fidget overtly; the small-object worry is contained within the hand and often invisible.

**Eating with hands.** Surprising delicacy. Pizza slice gripped at the crust with three fingers, never four. He has learned to hold a fork using only the very tips of his thumb and index, the way a man might handle a needle. Coffee cups are held with one finger crooked through the handle and the others spread away — the handle would shatter under his palm.

---

## V. EATING, DRINKING, AND ORAL CONSUMPTION

Caloric requirement is estimated at 12,000–18,000 kcal/day baseline, higher under combat load. Food is unambiguously the primary scheduled pleasure of his day.

**Eating posture.** Sits forward at the table, elbows often on the surface, head close to the plate. This is partly olfactory deficit compensation — he leans in to get more aromatic signal — and partly an old neighborhood-table habit from a childhood where food was protected as it was consumed.

**Pace.** Quick early in a meal, slowing toward the end. The first quarter of any meal is consumed with focused attention and almost no talking; from the second quarter onward he becomes conversational. He will offer food from his plate to others by sliding the plate or pushing items toward them rather than gesturing with utensils — a learned hospitality from Petunia's kitchen.

**Signature consumption.** Pizza (the operational reference food, Yancy Street pedigree); pastrami on rye (the standing order at Klein's-style delis throughout Manhattan); diner breakfasts with the full plate sequence — eggs, multiple meats, potatoes, toast, coffee; Petunia's pot roast as the emotional gold standard; Sheckerberg-style appetizing food (lox, whitefish, bagels) which became more visible in his diet after the explicit return to Jewish practice; chinese takeout in the loft late at night, eaten standing at the counter. He does not, despite expectation, gravitate to "huge man-food" — steaks and ribs are present but not dominant. He likes carbs and salt; he likes food that *smells*; he does not love sweets (the gustatory deficit hits sugar discrimination harder than salt).

**Beer.** One to three, almost always domestic and almost always from a bottle (he cannot reliably grip a can without crushing it; he can but does not bother). Drinks slowly. Has been observed nursing a single beer for two hours during a family dinner. Will refuse a fourth more often than accept. This is intentional and lifelong — the paternal alcoholic shadow is the relevant variable.

**Coffee.** Black, large volume, hot, throughout the day. Holds the mug with one finger.

**Cigars.** Historical only. Phased out in the late 1960s; occasional ceremonial use (a victory, a wedding, the birth of Valeria) but not a habit.

**Eating under stress.** Increases volume and decreases speed-of-consumption — chews longer, swallows slower, seems to derive less pleasure. He notices this in himself and will sometimes push the plate away mid-meal, which is the most reliable somatic distress signal short of withdrawal from the room.

**Eating in intimacy.** With Alicia, he slows further. He has been observed feeding her — gently, with a fork held in the very tips of his fingers — at home dinners. This is one of the few unguardedly tender behaviors in his repertoire.

---

## VI. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Position.** Sleeps on his back. The mass and dermal plating make side-sleep mechanically punishing on bed-frames; he learned this in the first week post-transformation by destroying two box springs. The reinforced bed in the Baxter Building (Reed-engineered, never discussed) supports the side-sleep he prefers but rarely uses.

**Duration.** Six to seven hours typically, less than the human male average for that mass. He does not appear to require more.

**Sleep onset.** Fast when calm — within ten to fifteen minutes of horizontal. Slow when troubled — he has been observed lying awake for two to three hours after a difficult day, eyes open, hands folded on his chest, not moving. The motionless wakefulness is characteristic and distinct from insomnia agitation: he does not toss, does not get up, does not reach for distraction. He simply waits the night out.

**Dreaming.** Confirmed across multiple narrative episodes. Dreams in human form more often than as the Thing — eyewitness reports (his own, mostly to Alicia) suggest the dreaming self has not fully updated to the post-transformation body. He wakes from these dreams quietly. There is no record of him crying out in sleep.

**Snoring.** Audible, rhythmic, deep. Has been remarked on as carrying through Baxter Building walls during shared-residence eras. He is aware and self-conscious about it.

**Pre-sleep ritual.** Reads in bed — paperbacks, often pulp adventure or military memoir, occasionally rabbinic commentary in the late-period. Reading glasses (a real necessity — the cosmic-ray transformation did not improve his close vision and may have worsened it) perched on the brow-plate, which is itself a moment of small daily comedy he has come to accept. Lamp off, glasses on the nightstand, hand passes once across the eyes, exhale, still.

**Waking.** Slowly. He sits up before standing — never the bolt-upright pre-form pilot's wake. First action almost always is a long exhale and a hand-rub across the face.

---

## VII. GROOMING AND BODILY MAINTENANCE

**Skin/dermal care.** The plates require occasional debris-clearance — small particulate gets caught in the seams. He performs this with a stiff brush in the shower. Has occasionally been observed using a putty knife for stubborn material with apparent indifference to sensation. The seams of the plates are mildly photogenic dark lines that he does not bother to address cosmetically.

**Showering.** Daily, water at maximum heat (his thermal tolerance is enormous; cooler water reads as cold to him). Standard duration ~8 minutes. He has destroyed multiple showerheads through inadvertent contact; the Baxter Building installation is fortified.

**Shaving.** Not required.

**Haircuts.** Not required.

**Teeth.** Brushes — the teeth remain organic-presenting and require maintenance. Uses an oversized brush head, mid-stiffness bristle, daily.

**Clothing.** Limited wardrobe by both physical constraint (off-the-rack will not fit) and preference (he is not vain about clothes). Standard uniform when on duty. Off-duty: oversized custom flannel or cotton button-downs in solid colors, dark trousers reinforced at the seat and thighs, very large soft-soled shoes or barefoot indoors. He prefers barefoot whenever socially permissible — the foot dermal plating gives him excellent floor-feedback and shoes are an irritation. At home he is almost always shoeless.

**Hats.** A trench coat and fedora ensemble — used historically as civilian camouflage during the first decade and a half, and revived occasionally for nostalgia or genuine privacy need. The hat sits low; the coat collar high. He knows the silhouette fools no one who is paying attention and uses it anyway.

**Jewelry/effects.** Wedding band custom-made and worn on the left ring finger — the band sized for the four-fingered hand. Otherwise nothing. Wristwatches do not survive his wrist.

---

## VIII. VOICE AND VOCAL BEHAVIOR

**Register.** Bass, ~85–110 Hz fundamental, with a chest resonance that is physically perceptible at close range — civilians have reported feeling his voice in their sternum during normal conversation. He has learned to modulate downward in volume to keep this from being intimidating.

**Accent.** Brooklyn — Yancy Street working-class Jewish, broad on the vowels, hard on the consonants, mid-twentieth-century vintage. He has *intensified* this over the decades rather than softened it. The accent is partly authentic and partly performed, and the performance ratio rises with audience.

**Cadence.** Quick when bantering, slow when serious. The serious-Ben voice loses most of the Brooklyn coloration and drops in pitch — the rhetorical effect is dramatic and reliably reorients a room. When he says "Reed" in the slow-low register, every member of the FF stops what they are doing.

**Vocal tics.** The "feh," the "ah, fer cryin' out loud," the "stretcho/matchstick/Susie-girl" diminutives, "what a revoltin' development," and of course the battle-cry. The battle-cry is delivered at a consistent volume and pitch across sixty years of canon — he treats it as a marker, not a war-shout; the volume is moderate. When he genuinely needs to hit something hard, he is silent.

**Silence.** He is comfortable in silence, more so than most of the FF. Will sit quietly with Alicia for long stretches. Will sit quietly with Reed in the lab, occupying a chair, not reading, not speaking, just present — this is one of the most consistent late-career somatic patterns and reads, correctly, as the most articulate statement of forgiveness in his repertoire.

---

## IX. STATE-DEPENDENT SHIFTS

A state-by-state mapping of the above baselines:

### Calm / domestic

Shoulders descend; head carriage straightens; brow-ridge tension drops; jaw unclenches; hands relax into the front-clasp or hip rest; voice softens by ~20 dB and loses Brooklyn coloration partially; movement slows; barefoot; tactile contact with Alicia or children frequent and unconscious. The smirk is absent; a softer half-smile is present. Breathing audible but deep and slow.

### Working / routine team operations

Posture squares; arms cross more often; brow neutral but engaged; the smirk is the dominant face; banter rate elevated; food and coffee intake high; movement efficient and purposeful. Hand cracks knuckles more. Voice in standard register with full Brooklyn coloration.

### Mild stress (1–3)

Vocal cadence quickens; jokes per minute increases noticeably; chewing rate increases at meals; right shoulder rolls more frequently; visible toe-tap or weight shift; coffee intake climbs.

### Significant stress (4–6)

Withdrawal initiates: subject leaves the room, the floor, or the building. Walking pace increases. Jaw clench becomes visible and sustained. Hands fold high across chest more often. Speech volume drops. Will seek out a workshop, a punching bag, the roof, or a low-stakes patrol route to discharge. Will not eat until the stress drops.

### Severe stress (7–8)

Full motor stillness in private moments — the motionless lying-awake pattern. In company, monosyllabic. Brow stays low. Touch-seeking from intimates is accepted but not initiated. May depart the geography entirely (the historical Battleworld/wrestling/Yancy escape pattern).

### Threat / combat readiness

Center of gravity drops perhaps two inches as the knees flex more deeply; weight balances perfectly across both feet; hands open and float at hip level; head comes up, eyes lock, brow drops; breathing deepens and slows; the smirk vanishes. Voice, if used, is quiet and clipped. The pre-engagement seconds are visually startling: the man becomes geological in stillness. The battle-cry, if used, follows the *decision* to engage by less than a half-second.

### Peak threat to loved ones

All vocalization ceases. Movement becomes economical to the point of seeming choreographed. The face goes flat — not angry, *flat*, which is the most dangerous face he has and the rarest. Adversaries who have seen this face and survived report it as the most frightening single observation in their careers. Post-event, within seconds of threat-neutralization, he moves immediately to the harmed party — kneels, lowers his voice to the private register, uses the back-of-fingers contact, asks one question ("y'okay?"), and waits.

### Intimacy (Alicia)

Every parameter softens. The mass-management discipline goes into its highest gear and


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: GRIMM, BENJAMIN JACOB
## SECTION 6 — ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

---

### 6.1 Attachment Classification and Developmental Origins

The subject's attachment organization is best classified as **earned secure with a chronic anxious-preoccupied undertow**, structured around an *internal working model* that can be stated almost as a syllogism: *the people I love die or leave; therefore I must stay; therefore I must be the kind of man who can be stayed with; therefore I must be useful, funny, and never the one who walks away first.* Every observable adult relational behavior is downstream of that proposition.

The developmental substrate is documented across forty-plus years of flashback material (Lee/Kirby establishment; Byrne's *FF* #259 and #277 origin elaborations; DeFalco's *Thing* solo run; Karl Kesel's "Remembrance of Things Past" arc, *FF* vol. 3 #56; the Slott-era Yancy Street flashbacks). The pattern is dense and over-determined:

- **Primary attachment figure (mother): dead, early.** Loss occurred in latency, before the subject had developed the cognitive scaffolding to grieve and reintegrate. The loss is *under-mentioned* by Ben in canon — a tell. Subjects who freely narrate a maternal loss have largely metabolized it; subjects who circle it without naming it have not. Ben rarely speaks of his mother. He speaks of his Aunt Petunia constantly, often in joke form. Displacement.
- **Primary identification figure (brother Daniel): killed in street violence, idolized.** Daniel is the ghost in every relationship. The subject inherited his gang, his street, his vocabulary, his cadence, and — most consequentially — the unspoken obligation to *be the one who lives well enough to justify the one who didn't*. Survivor guilt operationalized as ambition.
- **Father: alive, dangerous, unreliable, intoxicated.** The single most consequential figure in the negative template. Ben's adult life can be read as a forty-year exhibition of *not-father*: doesn't drink to excess, doesn't strike loved ones, doesn't disappear, doesn't fail to provide, doesn't humiliate the small. Reaction formation on a generational scale.
- **Compensatory caregivers (Uncle Jake, Aunt Petunia): stable, kind, late.** Jake is a physician — the *healer*, the man whose competence is exercised on bodies. That Ben's eventual closest bond is with another man whose competence is also exercised on bodies (Reed) is not coincidence. Jake is the *internal working model of the safe powerful man*, and Reed steps into that template with the cosmic-ray flight serving as the betrayal that the template was always braced for.

The developmental prediction from this substrate would be **disorganized or anxious-preoccupied attachment with depressive features and significant relational volatility**. What we observe instead — stable sixty-year bonds, a single durable marriage, sustained co-parenting, mature defenses — is the product of a *deliberate, decades-long compensatory project* whose principal materials are: the found family of the FF, the Masters bond, Jewish practice reclaimed in midlife, mentorship of children, and the disciplined suppression of paternal inheritance. The security is *earned* in the precise technical sense: built against the substrate, not given by it.

---

### 6.2 The Relational Template

A single template recurs across every significant relationship in the file. It runs in five phases:

**Phase 1 — Approach via Roughness.** Initial contact is conducted in gruff register: insult, mock-challenge, "ya little punk," "stretcho," "matchstick," a shoulder-jostle, a refusal of softness. This is *not* hostility. It is a stress-test administered to determine whether the other party can tolerate his actual surface (which is the rock surface in literal as well as figurative form). The roughness *is* the offer: *here is the worst of me first, so you cannot later claim I misrepresented.*

**Phase 2 — Observation of Response.** Those who flinch, condescend, or pity are catalogued and held at a polite middle distance — never cruelly, but permanently. Those who push back in kind, who laugh, or who fail to perform fear are admitted to the next phase. (This is why his bond with Johnny is structurally stronger than with most teammates: Johnny passed the test the first day and has been passing it for sixty years.)

**Phase 3 — Provisional Care, Plausibly Deniable.** Acts of service begin: showing up, lifting heavy things, fetching coffee, taking the dangerous tour of duty, charity gestures performed via "Aunt Petunia" cover stories, anonymous donations to Yancy Street youth programs. He is at this stage *intensely* generous in deed and *intensely* deflective in language. The phrase pattern "ain't no big deal" / "fergit it" / "shaddap" is the verbal seal placed over the act so it cannot be discussed.

**Phase 4 — Acceptance of Mutual Dependence (Reluctant).** Only after long observation does he allow the other party to do something *for* him and not deflect it away. This is the hardest phase for him; he is far more comfortable as the giver than the receiver. Receiving comfort, in particular, is somatically difficult — he physically braces, looks away, makes a joke. Alicia is the only person in the file who has consistently broken through this barrier; Sue is the second; Reed is third, and only in extremity.

**Phase 5 — Integration and Permanent Loyalty.** Once admitted, the bond is essentially non-revocable. Ben does not *un-love*. The bond can be wounded (the Reed cure-withholding wound; the AIM-era Sharon deterioration) and the subject can withdraw geographically, but the affective bond remains intact through the withdrawal and is the engine of the eventual return. He has never abandoned a person he reached Phase 5 with. This is the most diagnostic single fact in the relational file.

---

### 6.3 The Reed Relationship: The Central Diagnostic Bond

If one wanted to understand the subject in one relationship, this is it. The Richards bond carries every contradiction in his organization and is therefore the load-bearing wall of his psyche.

**Origin:** College roommates, State University. Class mismatch (working-class Lower East Side and rumpled Midwestern academic-aristocracy son), intellect mismatch (Reed's IQ off-scale, Ben's high-normal practical genius), temperament mismatch (Reed abstract, Ben concrete). The friendship works *because of* the mismatch, not despite: Ben gives Reed access to a body and a street and a register Reed cannot otherwise reach, and Reed gives Ben access to a future the Lower East Side does not offer. Each is the other's portal.

**The promise.** "Anytime, anywhere" — a casual collegiate vow that was, characteristically of Ben, *meant*. The cosmic-ray flight is the cashing-in of a promise made by a younger man who did not anticipate the price. That Ben was the one to *object* to the radiation risk and was overruled is the founding asymmetry. He was right; he paid; Reed was wrong; Reed paid less. This asymmetry has never fully closed.

**The wound that does not heal.** The "Reed could have cured me earlier and chose not to" beat (recurrent from the early DeFalco/Byrne run forward) is the single permanent injury in the bond. Ben has explicitly forgiven it multiple times and the forgiveness is real, but the wound is reactivatable under stress and any sufficiently informed adversary could weaponize it. (See §5 pressure points.)

**The repair mechanism.** What keeps the bond intact across sixty years is not that the wound closed but that *both parties verbalize and re-verbalize*. Ben says it: at the dinner table, in the lab, mid-fight. Reed receives it, sometimes badly, sometimes well, but receives it. Ben says it again. Reed eventually responds with the small, awkward, kinesthetic gestures of affection he is capable of — a hand on the shoulder, an apology phrased as a technical observation, a quietly performed favor. Ben accepts the gesture. The cycle resets. This is a model of **chronic-wound, high-function bond maintenance** and is rarer in the canon than it appears.

**The Yancy Street Gang as displacement valve.** The endless, decades-running gag of the Yancy Street Gang pranking Ben is, on the surface, comic relief. In the relational file it is *the displacement mechanism that protects the Reed bond*. The hostility Ben cannot direct at Reed without destroying the family is decanted into a tolerated, almost cherished antagonism with a target that cannot be hurt and cannot leave. Many of the pranks have been revealed across the canon to be, at various times, Johnny — which is itself diagnostic: the family understands at some level that Ben needs the valve and provides it.

**Operational implication.** Ben will follow Reed into any cosmic situation. Ben will *not* follow Reed into ethical compromise — the post-*Civil War* rupture, in which Ben left the country rather than enforce the SHRA, is the cleanest example. The bond is unconditional in affection and entirely conditional in obedience. This is the mark of a securely-attached subordinate, not a fused one.

---

### 6.4 The Sue Relationship: The Sister-Bond

Susan Storm Richards functions in the file as the **adopted sister and emotional translator**. She is the figure to whom Ben confides what he cannot say to Reed (because saying it to Reed would be an accusation) and what he cannot say to Johnny (because Johnny would weaponize it into a joke).

The bond is notably *non-romantic*, *non-rivalrous*, and *quietly load-bearing*. Ben is, with Sue, more articulate, less performative, and visibly softer in cadence. He drops the Brooklyn schtick at about 30% — never fully, but more than with anyone else in the team. He has, across the canon, been the one to notice first when Sue is wounded by Reed's coldness and the one to intervene with Reed on her behalf. He has lifted her physically out of multiple situations with a kind of automatic, fraternal carefulness. He calls her "Suzie" — diminutive, familial, fixed.

The template-fit: Sue occupies the slot that would have been Daniel's, in the inverse direction — the *sibling he protects* rather than the sibling who protected him. The reparative function is obvious. He failed to save Daniel. He will not fail to save Sue. The unstated vow operates continuously.

---

### 6.5 The Johnny Relationship: The Sibling Who Lived

Where Sue is the sister he protects, Johnny is the *brother he gets to keep*. The Storm-Grimm dyad is the most affectively expressive bond in the file — pranks, insults, physical roughhousing, immediate reconciliation. It is also the bond in which Ben permits himself the most regression: with Johnny he is closer to seventeen than sixty, and the regression is restorative. This is a man who lost his older brother in childhood being permitted to play *younger brother* with his younger brother for sixty years. The therapeutic function is enormous and largely unconscious to both parties.

When Johnny has been believed dead or lost (*FF* #587 and aftermath, Hickman run), Ben's grief presentation is the most acute and least defended in the entire canon. He does not joke. He does not deflect. He sits with the loss as he could not sit with Daniel's. The defenses *fail* in the right way — meaning the bond has reached a depth where defense is no longer organizing the affect. This is, clinically, an excellent sign for the integration of the original sibling loss; he has been *permitted to mourn properly* via a substitute attachment that survived long enough to be lost in adulthood with full faculties intact.

The pranks-and-counterpranks pattern is the *operational signature* of the bond. It is the same approach-via-roughness pattern as everywhere else in his file, but with the dial turned to maximum on both sides — a relational shorthand that signals continuous mutual presence without ever requiring the vocabulary of love. Both parties know what the pranks mean. Neither will say it aloud. This is consistent with the family-of-origin script and with the working-class-male affective vocabulary the subject has never abandoned.

---

### 6.6 The Alicia Relationship: The Bond That Re-Wrote the Template

Alicia Masters is the single most consequential figure in the subject's relational reorganization. The bond is *foundationally structured around her blindness*, and the structure must be assessed honestly rather than sentimentally.

**Why blindness matters, clinically.** Ben's body-image disturbance (see §4) has at its core the conviction that he is *visually unlovable*. Alicia cannot see him. The bond is therefore initially safe in a way no other adult intimate bond can be safe: the perceiver cannot make the perception that he most fears. This is not health. It is, however, *stabilization* — a relational structure in which intimacy becomes possible at all. Without Alicia or someone occupying her structural slot, the subject's romantic life would likely have remained foreclosed.

**Why the bond has become healthy across the decades.** What began as defense has, over forty years of canon, evolved into something genuinely integrated. Alicia *knows* what he looks like through touch and through the descriptions of others. She has chosen him repeatedly with that knowledge. The structural safety of her blindness has provided enough relational scaffolding for Ben to *experience being loved as the Thing*, which has slowly eroded the conviction that he cannot be. The marriage works because Alicia did the work of seeing him as he is and Ben did the work of *believing she had done so*. The latter is the harder work, and the longer.

**Intimacy patterns.** With Alicia he is unguarded in private and physically extraordinarily careful. The strength-modulation is constant and unconscious; he has not, in canon, ever harmed her physically, despite holding her thousands of times. He lets her touch his face. This is the highest-trust act in his somatic repertoire and is reserved almost exclusively for her. He has been observed (Slott, Waid runs) to *close his eyes* when she does so — a behavioral marker indicating the gesture is being received with full affective load and that he does not want her to see (or sense) his face in the moment.

**The proposal-delay pattern.** Across the canon Ben repeatedly delays formalizing the relationship via the same script: *she deserves better.* This is the public, charitable framing of an internal proposition that runs: *if I marry her I have to believe I am marriable.* Each delayed proposal is therefore not about Alicia at all; it is about the lag between his external situation (loved) and his internal self-concept (unlovable). The eventual marriage is the formal closure of that lag, and it has held.

**The chronic grief beneath the bond.** That he cannot feel her with the discrimination of human skin is a daily wound. The canon depicts this directly and indirectly across multiple writers; the recurrence of "feeling her face" panels is not sentimentality but pattern-display. He has metabolized the grief into a structured tolerance, but it does not resolve. This is the cost of the bond, and he pays it.

---

### 6.7 The Children: Franklin, Valeria, Jo-Venn, N'Kalla

The relationship to children — particularly Franklin and Valeria Richards, and in late canon his adopted Jo-Venn and N'Kalla — is the cleanest, least conflicted relational territory in the file. With children he is *un-defended*. The schtick recedes; the gentleness comes forward; the strength is modulated to near-zero contact pressure; the vocabulary becomes warmer and more inflected with the Lower East Side rather than less.

The reparative function is overdetermined: he is being to these children every adult he wishes he had had — the present uncle (Jake), the safe man, the funny man, the man who does not drink and does not strike and does not leave. He is also being to them *what he was not able to be to Daniel*, which is the older protector who *succeeds*. The protection-of-children imperative (§5, #1 drive) is sourced here. Threats to Franklin and Valeria reliably produce his most controlled and most lethal-grade operational responses.

Worth noting: the children, particularly Valeria, *know* him with great clarity. Valeria is intellectually her father's daughter but emotionally Ben's; she has read his moods accurately since toddlerhood and treats him with the offhand affection that signals she has never doubted the bond. This unguarded acceptance by a child of Reed's lineage is one of the quiet repairs of the Reed-wound. *Reed's daughter loves him without reservation.* The transitive arithmetic is not lost on him.

---

### 6.8 The Sharon Ventura Relationship: The Counter-Example

The Sharon Ventura (Ms. Marvel II / She-Thing) arc during the DeFalco solo run is the file's most important counter-example and must be assessed without sanitization. The relationship was sourced in *shared somatic catastrophe* — she mutated into a Thing-form during the AIM kidnapping arc — and it did not survive that sourcing. The bond was not built via the Phase 1–5 template above; it was forged in crisis and never tested in stability. Both parties were using each other as mirrors of monstrousness, and the mirror function collapsed under sustained weight.

**What it tells us:** Ben's relational pattern requires *time* and the slow stress-test of the template. Bonds formed in acute trauma without the slow approach phase do not stabilize for him. He cannot bond properly via crisis-fusion. This is consistent with secure-attachment functioning and inconsistent with the borderline-organization style of crisis-bonding. The Sharon arc, painful as it was, is therefore *good news* for his structural diagnosis.

---

### 6.9 The Mentor Pattern

The subject is a serial, low-key mentor. The pattern: identifies a younger figure who is struggling with the integration of power and identity; performs gruff dismissal; conducts surveillance from a discreet distance; intervenes at the critical moment with a combination of practical instruction, moral framing, and a deliberately under-stated affirmation that the younger figure is *worth* the trouble.

Recipients include, across the canon: early-career Spider-Man (the team-up pattern in *Marvel Team-Up* is a sustained example), the original Ms. Marvel, the Future Foundation children collectively, various Yancy Street youth in charity contexts, and, in a particular and unspoken way, Johnny — Ben's mentorship of Johnny is the longest-running of all and is conducted entirely through the prank-vocabulary.

The mentor pattern *is the Daniel pattern inverted*. Ben was the younger brother under the older brother's protection; he now occupies the older brother slot toward everyone smaller, younger, or earlier in the process. This is one of the cleanest sublimations in the file.

---

### 6.10 Distrust, Betrayal, and Repair

**Distrust signature.** Ben distrusts *slowly* and *visibly*. He does not run hidden suspicion. When he begins to distrust a figure, the body-language shifts before the language does: shoulders square slightly more, the jokes become harder-edged, the eye-contact lengthens, the proximity decreases by a measurable foot or two. This is observable to any trained observer and is, in operational terms, a *tell* — but it is also a kind of integrity. He will not pretend to trust whom he does not.

**Response to betrayal.** Withdraws geographically rather than retaliating. The Battleworld decision, the post-Reed-cure-revelation departure, the post-*Civil War* expatriation — all are the same pattern. He removes himself from proximity rather than do or say something irrevocable. This is mature defense functioning of a high order; few subjects in the file regulate aggression this consistently against persons they love.

**Repair signature.** Returns. Always returns.
