Tracks Franklin's and Valeria's locations even in fully secure environments. Has been observed, multiple times, sleeping on a couch outside the children's quarters when threat-level is elevated.

**Discipline.** Soft. Will deflect to Sue or Reed for actual rule-enforcement. The few times he has directly disciplined a child it has been quiet, brief, and immediately followed by physical reassurance.

---

### 6.8 INTIMACY (REED — the diagnostic relationship)

**Approach pattern.** Bluster-forward. Walks into Reed's lab loudly, announces himself with insult (*hey, stretcho; whatcha cookin', egghead; gimme that*), inserts himself physically into Reed's workspace, often *handles Reed's equipment* in a way that reads as harassment and functions as connection. This is the language of their fifty-year college-roommate dialect and neither has updated it.

**Listening pattern.** Despite the patter, listens to Reed with full attention. Will let Reed monologue technical material without interruption, then summarize back in plain English — Reed's tell that Ben is tracking is that Ben restates the operational implication. Reed needs this; Ben provides it without acknowledgment.

**Touch.** Rare and significant. A hand on Reed's shoulder is a moment of high emotional weight in any scene it appears. The arm around Reed's shoulders is reserved for victory, grief, and reconciliation.

**Conflict.** When angry at Reed, he does not joke. The absence of the Brooklyn schtick directed at Reed is the alarm signal. Confrontations are direct, verbal, and conducted at lower volume than his stress-bluster — Reed-confrontations are the most controlled rage in his catalog. Resolves with a beer, a handshake, sometimes a hug. Rupture-and-return cycles are part of the bond's structural integrity.

---

### 6.9 INTIMACY (JOHNNY — younger-brother register)

**Mode.** Continuous low-grade hazing, which Johnny returns in kind, and which both use as a circulatory system for genuine affection neither will state directly. The pranks (the Yancy Street Gang's harassment is largely Johnny-orchestrated and Ben knows it and pretends not to) are a vocabulary.

**Under threat to Johnny.** All of it disappears instantly. Ben will fly across continents and into stars for Johnny without comment and resume the hazing the moment Johnny is safe. The pattern is exact and has been repeated dozens of times.

---

### 6.10 INTIMACY (SUE — sister-figure register)

**Mode.** Respectful, slightly courtly, the only FF member Ben consistently softens his language around. Calls her Suzie, but rarely teases her directly. Defers to her in domestic decisions. Sue is the person he goes to when he cannot go to Alicia and will not go to Reed; the canon has shown this conversation more times than is generally noted.

---

### 6.11 GRIEF

**Public grief (combat losses, civilian losses, allies).** Quiet. Stands at the back of rooms. Removes himself from group settings within ~20 minutes. Will be found later on a roof. Does not weep in the presence of others if he can help it.

**Private grief (Alicia injured, Reed missing/dead, a child harmed, Aunt Petunia's death, Daniel-memory triggers).** Has been observed by intimates in three distinct grief postures: (1) seated on a reinforced bench or floor, elbows on knees, hands hanging, head down — the *waiting* posture; (2) standing at a window, back to the room, arms folded — the *blocking* posture; (3) walking, slowly, alone, for hours, often through the old neighborhood — the *moving* posture, which appears to be the most effective for him.

**Ritual grief.** Lights yahrzeit candles for his mother, his brother Daniel, and (post-canonical-disclosure) for his murdered neighbor Mr. Sheckerberg. Says Kaddish — the Slott-era and Aguirre-Sacasa-era runs establish this as a recurring practice. The faith arc has given him a *structured* grief vocabulary he did not have for the first forty years of the canon, and the behavioral difference is observable: late-career grief is more contained, more durative, less prone to triggering withdrawal cascades.

**Anniversary behavior.** Tracks the date of the cosmic-ray flight without acknowledging that he is tracking it. On or near that date he is quieter, eats less, more likely to be found on the roof. Sue has noticed; Reed has noticed; neither raises it. Alicia raises it gently and is the only one allowed to.

---

### 6.12 VICTORY

**Public.** Loud. The catchphrase is deployed in retrospect — *told ya it was clobberin' time* — usually with a fist-pump or a grabbed-Johnny-in-a-headlock celebration. Will accept the crowd. Signs autographs (he is *good* with crowds, better than Reed by an order of magnitude). Photo-ops are tolerated with practiced patience.

**Private.** Substantially more muted. Will sit down heavily and exhale. Reaches for food. Reaches for Alicia. Does not gloat in private; gloating is performance. The internal cost of any major engagement is visible to intimates in the ~hour after extraction — he is *tired* in a way he does not show in the field.

**Toward the defeated.** Does not humiliate. Will extend a hand to a beaten foe more often than any other FF member. There is a specific tell: post-combat, if the enemy is human and not actively dangerous, his hands will go to his hips or fold across his chest — a *standing down* posture that adversaries learn to recognize. Doom and Annihilus-class enemies do not get this courtesy.

---

### 6.13 DEFEAT

**In-mission defeat (team loss, civilian casualty, missed save).** Immediate self-blame, often vocalized: *shoulda been faster, shoulda been there, shoulda took the hit.* Will replay the engagement in his head visibly — eyes drift, jaw works. Will not eat for several hours, an anomaly significant against his baseline. Will seek out the bereaved or the survivor before debriefing the team. The order of operations is reliable: comfort, then debrief, then withdraw.

**Personal defeat (reversion failure, Reed-disclosure trauma, public humiliation, mirror moments).** The bottom-band response. Withdraws fully. Goes to a roof. Will sometimes punch through inanimate objects (walls of abandoned buildings, derelict cars on a junkyard run) — controlled property destruction in unpopulated environments. This is the only context in which his aggression slips its sublimation and even then it is target-discriminated to property he has permission, implicit or explicit, to destroy.

**Existential defeat (the *what am I* moment — recurs every few years).** The longest withdrawals. The Battleworld decision. The wrestling-circuit era. Returns when someone — almost always Alicia, sometimes Reed, sometimes Aunt Petunia, once Spider-Man, once a child — articulates the case for his return in a language he cannot dismiss. The reliable solvent is being *needed by a specific person by name*. Abstract appeals fail; specific appeals always work.

---

### 6.14 ROUTES, ROUTINES, RITUALS

**Daily.** Wakes early (pre-Reed, often pre-Sue). Coffee. Newspaper, paper edition where available — a generational tic he has not surrendered. Walks the perimeter of whatever the current HQ is; this is a security sweep he conducts without framing it as one. Breakfast, large. Workshop check-in with Reed. Training-room or vehicle-bay time. Mid-day food. Operational tasks. Evening with Alicia. Late-night roof time, frequently with a beer, often alone, occasionally with Johnny.

**Weekly.** Yancy Street visit — varies in length, never skipped for more than two weeks. Charity work, often anonymous (the canonical pattern of paying for a kid's surgery, a family's rent, a community center's repairs without leaving a name). Synagogue attendance in late-career canon, irregular but real.

**Annual.** Cosmic-ray anniversary (private, unacknowledged). High Holy Days observance, post-faith-arc. Daniel's yahrzeit. Mother's yahrzeit. Father's yahrzeit (the most complicated — observed, but his observance is noticeably shorter and his affect afterward noticeably darker). Aunt Petunia's birthday — a phone call, no fail. The FF founding anniversary — Reed sometimes notes it; Ben pretends not to care; Sue arranges dinner; Ben shows up early.

---

### 6.15 IDIOSYNCRASIES AND MICRO-TELLS — index

- The thumb-to-index tactile self-check (involuntary, hourly).
- The neck-crack sequence (left, right, shoulder


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: GRIMM, BENJAMIN JACOB
## Section 6: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

---

A surveillance week on Subject Grimm yields one of the most legibly patterned files in the metahuman registry. He is a creature of route, hour, and ritual to a degree that surprises observers who expect chaos from a man whose body is a daily emergency. The opposite is true: precisely *because* the body is a daily emergency, the day around it is regimented. Order is his answer to entropy. What follows is a composite reconstruction from longitudinal observation, residential telemetry from the Baxter Building (and, in earlier eras, Pier 4 and Four Freedoms Plaza), debriefs of FF support staff, and pattern analysis of his civilian movement across Manhattan.

---

### A. The Pre-Dawn Hour (approx. 04:45–06:30)

Subject wakes early and without an alarm. Sleep onset is typically 23:30–00:30; total sleep ~5.5 hours, which appears sufficient — the dermal substrate seems to reduce recovery requirements. He wakes on his back, lies still for 90–180 seconds (observed via thermal/movement signatures), and then sits at the edge of the bed for a further interval with both hands flat on his thighs. This is the **morning audit** — a quiet, eyes-open re-inventory of the body. He has done this every morning since approximately 1962. There is no evidence he is aware it is a ritual.

He does not look at the bedroom mirror on the way out. The mirror in the master bath was, per renovation records, repositioned at his request in the late 1980s so that it does not face the door; he approaches it laterally, uses it for shaving (he still goes through the motions with an electric razor on the upper lip and jaw — there is no stubble to remove, but the act is preserved), and exits without the head-on look. **Mirror avoidance** is the single most stable somatic micro-pattern in the file.

Coffee is brewed first — Bustelo, made strong, no measuring; the scoop is by feel and consistent within 5% across hundreds of observations. He drinks it black from an oversized mug (capacity ~24 oz; the standard 12-oz mug is structurally inadequate to his grip and he has cracked many). The first cup is consumed standing at the kitchen window, facing east. He does not sit for it. The second cup, if it occurs, he takes to the workshop or the gym.

---

### B. Morning Physical Discipline (06:30–08:30)

Subject trains daily. This is non-negotiable and has been documented from at least 1965 forward. The form varies — heavy bag work, sled-pulling against calibrated resistance plates designed by Reed (the resistance has had to be revised upward seven times since 1971), swimming in the reinforced sub-basement pool — but the *occurrence* does not. Skip days are rare and correlate without exception to (a) active off-world deployment, (b) post-injury recovery from a Class 5+ event, or (c) the immediate aftermath of an Alicia-related crisis.

The training is not for strength maintenance — his strength is not training-dependent. It is for **kinesthetic calibration**. He works on touch, on the gradient between a half-pound press and a forty-ton press, on the difference between catching an egg and catching a car. The egg drill is real and observed: a tray of raw eggs on the workshop bench, transferred one at a time between hands, occasionally tossed, occasionally caught one-handed mid-step. Yield rate, last sampled: 94%. This is how he stays able to touch his wife, his children, and the small things of the world. The drill predates the marriage by decades.

Boxing footwork, learned originally in the Air Force and refined through the unlimited-class wrestling years, remains visible — he shadowboxes for 8–12 minutes on most mornings, weight on the balls of the feet despite his mass, lead hand higher than orthodox would prefer. He talks to himself during this, low volume, mostly trash-talk to imaginary opponents but occasionally — per audio captures — to Doom, to Annihilus, and on at least three occasions to his father.

---

### C. The Breakfast Problem (08:30–09:15)

Food is one of his preserved pleasures and the routine reflects it. Breakfast is large, structured, and eaten *with people* whenever possible. The standing menu, varied but recognizable across decades:

- Eggs (six, scrambled, soft)
- A meat — bacon, pastrami, lox depending on day and observance
- Bagel from a specific Yancy-adjacent bakery; deliveries logged three mornings a week, the other days he picks up in person on the walk back from a route described below
- Fruit — bananas, almost ritually; this is the one piece of dietary advice from his uncle Jake that has stuck
- A second pot of coffee

If Alicia is present he eats slowly; if alone he eats quickly. If the children are present he eats theatrically — narrating, performing, making faces. The performance is for them and is a deliberate (though probably unexamined) act of teaching them that the body at the table is safe and funny rather than frightening. They have grown up with this. They do not flinch.

Kashrut observance is *partial and increasing*. Post-2002 (the Sheckerberg arc onward) the household keeps loose kosher — no pork in the apartment, separation of meat and dairy at the table though not in the kitchen, escalating observance on the holidays. He is not strict on the road. The bacon, when it appears, appears at diner counters, not at home. This is a meaningful distinction to him.

---

### D. The Yancy Walk

Three to five mornings a week, weather and threat-board permitting, Subject leaves the Baxter Building on foot and walks south. Route varies in the middle but the endpoints do not: he begins at the residential entrance, ends at a circuit of Lower East Side blocks that map onto his childhood. The walk takes 70–110 minutes one-way; he frequently catches a cab back or, in the modern era, is collected by Fantasti-Car drop.

The walk has several stations:

1. **The bakery.** Order is the same. He overpays. The owner, third-generation, refuses to acknowledge the overpay and Subject refuses to acknowledge the refusal. This dance is approaching its twentieth year.
2. **A specific stoop on Yancy Street** — not the building he was raised in (that building is gone) but the one across from where it stood. He sits for between four and twenty minutes. He does not visibly do anything. Observers have logged this stop hundreds of times. He has never been seen to cry there; he has been seen to laugh quietly twice.
3. **The synagogue.** He does not always enter. When he does, it is brief — five to fifteen minutes, usually mid-week and outside service hours. He is on first-name terms with the rabbi. He pays for things and asks that his name not be on them.
4. **The school yard.** He times the walk, on at least one morning a week, to coincide with recess at the elementary school nearest his old block. He does not approach. He stands across the street, watches for ten minutes, and moves on. This has been documented since at least 1998. It is not, per all behavioral indicators, sinister; it is the pattern of a man checking that the children of his old neighborhood are still alive and laughing where his brother is not.

The Yancy Street Gang "harassment" — graffiti, prank deliveries, the occasional flaming bag — occurs along this route and Subject's response is, invariably, performed outrage masking visible pleasure. The gang is in some non-trivial sense the only continuous institution of his pre-transformation life and he has effectively subsidized it for decades through anonymous channels.

---

### E. The Working Day (10:00–18:00, highly variable)

The Baxter "work" day is structurally elastic and has three modes:

**Mode 1 — Lab support.** Subject is in Reed's lab as muscle, sounding board, and human-scale brake. He does not pretend to follow the physics. He follows the *Reed*: watches face, watches breathing, watches whether Reed has eaten, intervenes when the science is about to override the conscience. His characteristic intervention is a single sentence delivered flatly, frequently a question framed as a request for clarification ("So just so I got this, Stretch — you're sayin' the kid stays in the box?"). This is one of the most consequential operational rituals in the file: he is the analog ethics review board on a man whose intellect routinely outruns his judgment. The intervention rate, by lab-log sampling, is approximately one substantive ethical flag per eleven hours of co-presence.

**Mode 2 — Mission/training.** Suit-up, briefing, deployment. Briefing posture: arms crossed, leaning on the back wall, last to speak and first to summarize. He restates the plan in plain English at the end of every briefing — a habit that began as accommodation for himself and that has become accommodation for everyone, including, increasingly, Reed.

**Mode 3 — Civilian life.** Errands, school pickup, charity appearances, the Yancy projects, occasional press. He drives when possible (a reinforced personal vehicle, customized seat, customized door pillar — the standard car door cannot survive a casual grab from him and he has learned to use two fingers on handles). He flies the Fantasti-Car for transit only when traffic compels it; he prefers the street, prefers being seen at street level, prefers being a neighbor.

Lunch, when not on mission, is a deli or a counter. He eats at a counter rather than a booth roughly 70% of the time — he can see the door, he doesn't crowd a booth, and the stool, reinforced or not, is replaceable. He is a generous tipper in cash, never card.

---

### F. The Children and the Domestic Evening

Between approximately 16:30 and 19:30 the surveillance signature shifts dramatically: Subject is **home-anchored** unless emergency overrides. School pickup if it is his day; homework supervision at the kitchen table (he is genuinely useful in history and useless in math, and has the self-awareness to call Valeria over when math arrives); cooking. He cooks. This is underreported in the public record. He grills, he braises, he makes the eggs his uncle Jake taught him. The kitchen is fortified — counters reinforced, a dedicated cast-iron set he can manipulate without crushing handles, knives selected for grip rather than balance.

Dinner with Alicia is the keystone of the day. The seating is fixed: she at one end, he kitty-corner rather than opposite, so that he can rest a hand on her forearm without reaching across the table. The hand-on-forearm is observed at approximately 80% of dinners and is the single most consistent intimate gesture in his repertoire — it is *his* tactile compensation, the place on her body where his diminished sensation matters least because the contact is grounding rather than exploratory. He has done this since the late 1960s.

After dinner: reading aloud to the children when they were younger; now, depending on configuration, board games (he is a ferocious and theatrical loser at Monopoly, a serene winner at chess despite the cliché), or television — older films, baseball, boxing. Subject does not watch news at home and has not since approximately 1985. This is a deliberate hygiene measure.

---

### G. Alicia, Specifically

The marriage runs on small, precisely calibrated tactile rituals because the medium of their intimacy *must* be calibrated. He sits next to her, not across. He announces movement in shared rooms — a low cleared throat, a footfall placed audibly — so that her spatial map updates without effort. He places objects she will reach for in fixed locations; this is so reflexive that visitors who rearrange a coffee mug are politely but firmly corrected.

Touch protocol: he leads with the back of the hand, not the palm — the back of the hand on a forearm, a shoulder, a cheek. The palm is reserved for moments where she has initiated. He has never, on record, initiated a hug. He receives them, fully and without flinch, and he reciprocates with what observers describe as a stillness that reads as held breath. He sleeps on his back; she sleeps with a hand on his chest. The bed is custom and reinforced; the linens are replaced more often than baseline due to abrasion.

Their conversation at home is heavily verbal — he describes things to her constantly, with a precision and an aesthetic vocabulary that is conspicuously absent from his public speech. The schtick is for the world; the sculptor's-grade descriptive language is for her. This bifurcation is one of the cleanest pieces of evidence in the file that the public Ben is a constructed presentation.

---

### H. Late Evening (21:30–23:30)

After the household settles, Subject's solitary rituals are observable:

- **The cigar.** Occasional, not daily — perhaps two evenings a week. On the roof or a balcony, never indoors. Held in the corner of the mouth, frequently unlit (the lighting is a separate ritual when it occurs; he uses a Zippo, snaps it closed with theatrical satisfaction, and the snap is the same snap from 1962 photographs). The cigar is a Yancy-era inheritance; it is also the only tobacco use in the file.
- **The beer.** One, sometimes two, never three. Bottled, never canned. Drinks slowly. The beer is a *signifier* — it announces to him and to anyone present that he is off-duty. He has, multiple times, declined a third because "the old man had a third." This is observed verbatim across decades.
- **Reading.** Pulp Westerns, war memoirs, increasingly Jewish theology and history (post-2002), and — observed with some surprise — poetry. He owns a battered copy of Yehuda Amichai and a battered copy of Whitman. He does not discuss either.
- **The workshop, late.** If unable to sleep he goes down, not up — to the workshop, not the roof. He fixes things. Small motors, neighbors' broken appliances (yes, neighbors leave them; yes, he returns them fixed; no, he does not charge), Valeria's experimental detritus. The fine-motor work is a continuation of the morning egg drill. It is also a way of being useful in silence.

He does not pray nightly in a formal sense. He does, with regularity that increased through the 2000s and has not retreated, murmur a brief Hebrew phrase before sleep. Audio captures are inconsistent but the cadence matches the Shema. He would not call this a prayer; he would call it "habit." The distinction is his to draw.

---

### I. The Weekly Cadence

A composite week:

- **Monday:** Lab-heavy. Yancy walk in the morning. Dinner at home. Late workshop.
- **Tuesday:** Training extended. Civilian errands. School pickup if rotation. Boxing on TV in the evening if anything is on.
- **Wednesday:** Variable — frequently a mission day historically. If quiet, charity appearance, often a hospital visit, almost always pediatric. He does not publicize these; the hospitals know to expect him; the children expect him; he is, on this point, a man of his word to a degree that approaches sacrament.
- **Thursday:** Yancy walk. Synagogue stop more probable. Dinner often includes Johnny, who maintains a near-standing invitation and uses it inconsistently. Subject sets a place anyway, every Thursday, observed for decades.
- **Friday:** Increasingly Shabbat-observant in form. Alicia lights candles; he says the blessing over the bread; the children are present when possible. Phone is set aside. The Baxter is informed that short of planetary emergency he is unavailable until Saturday evening. Compliance is imperfect and the world is unkind to the observance, but the *attempt* is the ritual.
- **Saturday:** Long-form family time. Park, museum (Alicia's choice, his pleasure), occasionally Coney Island, which is a pilgrimage site for him in ways he has never articulated.
- **Sunday:** Football (the Giants, suffered through). Cooking project. Reed-and-Sue dinner at the Baxter at variable cadence, hosted by Sue, attended by all under penalty of Sue's displeasure, which is the only authority Subject reliably defers to without negotiation.

---

### J. Micro-Patterns and Tells (Surveillance-Grade)

A non-exhaustive catalog of granular signatures a week of observation would log:

- **The door-frame check.** On entering any new room, brief touch of the top of the door-frame with the right hand — testing whether he fits, a habit dating to the early years when he frequently did not. He still does it. He no longer needs to.
- **The two-finger handle.** All door handles, faucet knobs, drawer pulls — index and thumb only, never full grip. Has become so automatic he uses two fingers on toothpicks.
- **The seated forward-lean.** In chairs (he uses reinforced seating at home and in the Baxter; in the wild, he leans forward with elbows on knees to keep his mass over his feet and off the chair). This is also a posture of attention — he is almost always listening when seated.
- **The voice-drop with children.** Public voice ~85 dB; child-directed voice drops to ~60 dB, with softened consonants and a Brooklyn cadence dialed down. Reverts immediately to baseline when the child leaves the room.
- **The pre-fight stillness.** Before combat, a 1–3 second total stillness, eyes closed or near-closed. This is not hesitation; it is the breath before "It's clobberin' time," which he uses sparingly and ritually rather than constantly. Observers have noted the catchphrase is reserved increasingly for moments he wishes to *signal* readiness to teammates rather than express it.
- **The post-fight check.** Within 90 seconds of combat end, eyes scan for civilians, then teammates, then self — in that order, every time.
- **The pocketing of small objects.** Coins, bottle caps, a child's lost button. He pockets things and forwards them later. Several times a year a Baxter housekeeper finds an envelope of recovered objects labeled in his blocky handwriting with the date and location of recovery.
- **The handwriting itself.** Block capitals, large, pressed hard enough to dent the paper. He prints; he does not cursive. He signs his name as "BEN GRIMM" rather than with a flourish, and the signature is the same in 1963 photographs and modern documents.
- **Phone behavior.** He uses a hardened, oversized device. He answers on the second ring, never the first (the first ring is, per his explanation to Franklin once, "rude to the caller — like you was waitin'"). He says "Yeah, Grimm" rather than "Hello." He ends calls with "Awright" and a hang-up; he does not say goodbye. Exception: Alicia, the children, Sue. With them he says goodbye.
- **The watch.** Wears one. Cannot wear a band — uses a pocket watch on a chain, his uncle Jake's, restored. Checks it perhaps three times a day. Time-keeping for him is mostly internal; the watch is a relic, not an instrument.
- **The Yancy hat.** A specific battered cap, kept in the front closet, worn on the Yancy walks and nowhere else. It is, per residence inventory, the oldest single item of his clothing still in active rotation.

---

### K. What a Week of Surveillance Would Conclude

That the subject lives a small life inside a large one. That for a man of planetary-scale capability, the operational center of gravity of his existence is a kitchen table, a stoop on Yancy Street, a hand on his wife's forearm, and a workshop bench with eggs on it. That the rituals are protective and the protection is *of others from him* as much as of him from the world — the two-finger handle and the audible footfall and the cigar on the balcony are all variations of the same prayer: *let me not break what I love*. That the day's structure is the visible architecture of a man who has, over six decades, built a livable life on top of a permanent emergency, and who maintains it the way one maintains a building on a fault line: with quiet daily attention, no grand gestures, and the unspoken understanding that the ground is not going to stop moving and the building must therefore be loved into staying upright every single morning.

The week ends as it began: pre-dawn audit, hands on thighs, the body inventoried, the day begun.

— UATU, recording.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: GRIMM, BENJAMIN JACOB
## SECTION 6 — RELATIONSHIPS I: FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

---

The Grimm family-of-origin file is, in conventional intelligence terms, a casualty list. Of the five blood relatives who occupied his Yancy Street apartment during his childhood, three were dead before he reached adolescence; one was the agent of much of the damage; one was lost to him by simple poverty (he was sent to live with an aunt and uncle, themselves childless, themselves working class, themselves the sole functional adults in his early environment). Everyone he calls family today — Alicia, Franklin, Valeria, the adopted children, Reed, Sue, Johnny — is *chosen*. The blood family is a graveyard against which the chosen family is silhouetted, and the silhouette is the whole shape of the man. This section maps the dead and the formative few; later sections map the chosen.

A pattern observable across every relationship below: Ben Grimm does not relinquish bonds. The dead are not past-tense in his interior life. He maintains them — visits graves, observes yahrzeit, reconstructs lost conversations, talks to them under his breath when alone in the cockpit or the workshop. A surveillance file with audio capture would log dozens of these unprompted, sotto-voce addresses per year, mostly to Daniel, occasionally to Jake, very rarely to his mother, never to his father.

---

### 6.1 — DANIEL GRIMM (Brother, deceased)

**Status:** Deceased c. early-to-mid 1940s, Yancy Street, gang-related violence. Subject was approximately seven to nine years old at time of death; Daniel was in his late teens. Body identified by subject and uncle. Circumstances: knife wound during territorial conflict between Yancy Street and a rival Lower East Side outfit. No prosecution. Case unresolved by NYPD; in the neighborhood economy of the period, also unresolved by retaliation, which became a private wound the subject carried for years.

**Historical function in the household.** Daniel was the operative parent. The biological father was either absent, drinking, or violent; the mother was overwhelmed and, by Ben's later description, frequently ill. Daniel ran the apartment in practical terms — meals, school enforcement, bruise-explanation — and he ran the street in the literal sense, as leader of the Yancy Street Gang in its pre-criminal iteration (a neighborhood protection outfit that crossed into petty crime as economic pressure mounted). To the young Ben, Daniel was simultaneously father, hero, employer, protector, and ideology. The subject's earliest moral framework — *you stand for your block, you don't rat, you hit back, you protect the smaller kid* — is Daniel's, transcribed verbatim and never substantively revised across eight decades.

**Cause of the bond's permanence.** Daniel was killed *before disappointing him*. The idealization had no time to attenuate through ordinary adolescent disillusionment. What would, in normal development, become a complicated and partially repudiated identification, instead froze at the worship stage. Every adult value the subject articulates can be traced either to Daniel's praxis or to a deliberate inversion of the father (see 6.3). Functionally, Daniel is the superego.

**Survivor-guilt structure.** The subject *escaped*. He got the football scholarship; he got the Air Force; he got the cosmic ray; he got the Baxter Building. Daniel got a knife. The asymmetry is, by his own intermittent admission across decades of dialogue, the original wound under all the others. The cosmic-ray transformation, in one available reading of Ben's interior logic, *corrected* the asymmetry: he no longer outpaced his brother. The body made him a Yancy Street kid again, marked and visible and unable to pass.

**Ongoing behavioral traces.** (a) Inability to walk past a fight between children without intervening; documented dozens of times across the canon, almost always with Yancy Street kids or analogues. (b) Disproportionate, often inarticulate fury when Franklin or Valeria are endangered by older agents — the threat-pattern matches Daniel's death (older predator, younger victim) and triggers an over-saturated response. (c) The Yancy Street Gang harassment running gag is, in the deep reading, *Daniel's gang refusing to let him forget where he came from* — and the subject's tolerance of and even affection for the harassment indicates he agrees with the verdict. He pays the gang's harassment as a kind of perpetual rent on his survival. (d) Recurrent dream content (referenced obliquely in dream-sequence stories): a younger brother he cannot reach.

**Trust/safety:** N/A (deceased). The internalized Daniel is wholly trusted. Subject will perform actions for the imagined approval of his dead brother that he will not perform for any living person.

**Failure mode:** When a current situation maps cleanly onto Daniel's death (older threatens younger; loyalty to neighborhood at stake; choice between escape and standing), the subject loses tactical flexibility and reverts to Daniel's code without modulation. This is exploitable in the sense that his behavior becomes predictable; it is not exploitable in the sense that it ever produces an unethical action — Daniel's code, however rigid, is morally clean.

**Leverage:** None directly usable. Attempting to invoke Daniel's memory manipulatively would be recognized as desecration and would produce a fixed, cold hostility from which no recovery is possible. Subject's own self-invocations of Daniel are the only legitimate currency.

---

### 6.2 — MOTHER (ELSIE GRIMM, née unspecified in canon; deceased)

**Status:** Deceased shortly after Daniel, c. late 1940s. Cause: variously implied as illness, exhaustion, "broken heart" in the subject's own narrative framing. Subject was approximately nine to eleven.

**Historical function.** Background presence rather than active parent in the subject's accessible memories — a function of both her overwhelmed circumstances and his coping. The depictions across canon are spare: a woman who worked, who was tired, who tried, who could not protect either son from the neighborhood or the husband, and who collapsed when Daniel was killed. The subject's affect when discussing her, on the rare occasions he does, is more tender than for any other origin figure, and also the most guarded. He uses her first name almost never.

**Internalized function.** The mother is the locus of a tenderness the subject permits himself only with Alicia and with children. There is reason to read his attraction to Alicia's *quality of suffered patience* — the calm with which she navigates a world that has been physically cruel to her — as partially mother-coded. The subject does not consciously frame it this way and would resist the framing; the pattern is nonetheless visible.

**Religious through-line.** Her Judaism, transmitted in the household before her death, is the rootstock of the subject's faith identity that resurfaces decades later in the Sheckerberg arc. The Shema he recites over the dying jeweler is, in the deep biography, his mother's Shema; she taught it to him before he was old enough to attend the bar mitzvah he later retroactively performs as an adult. The 2002 reaffirmation is, in part, a forty-year-overdue gift to her ghost.

**Ongoing behavioral traces.** (a) An unforced gentleness in the presence of older Jewish women that observers consistently note and that the subject does not consciously deploy. (b) Reflexive deference toward exhausted mothers in civilian-rescue contexts; will carry a child without asking, will not let a mother walk if she is wavering. (c) A specific food-pattern: certain dishes (kasha varnishkes, brisket, anything Ashkenazi-Jewish home-cooking adjacent) produce a flat, quiet, faraway eating manner distinct from his usual gusto. He eats them slowly. He does not joke through them.

**Trust/safety:** N/A. Internalized object is uncomplicatedly safe — possibly the only origin figure to whom this applies.

**Failure mode:** A subject-of-protection who maps onto the mother (exhausted, Jewish, working-class woman in a domestic-violence context) will receive his unconditional and possibly tactically-imprudent intervention.

**Leverage:** None usable without grave moral cost to user. Invoking her would be felt as a violation of something the subject has not even fully articulated to himself.

---

### 6.3 — FATHER (DANIEL GRIMM SR., deceased)

**Status:** Deceased, year and cause variable across continuity; alcohol-related decline is the consistent implication. Subject's relationship had functionally ended years prior, when he was sent to live with his uncle Jake.

**Historical function.** The agent of the household's destabilization. Alcoholic, intermittently employed, intermittently violent — verbally certainly, physically by clear implication in the more candid flashback work. Was alive when Daniel was killed and could not absorb the loss; the subject's mother died in the wake; the father continued drinking and disintegrating, and the surviving child was extracted to the uncle's apartment.

**Internalized function.** The negative template. Every adult discipline the subject maintains is the photographic negative of his father's example. The light drinking (beer only, no escalation, no use to manage affect); the iron suppression of aggression toward loved ones (Alicia, the children, the team — he will withdraw from a building before he will direct anger at them); the refusal to abandon his marriage or his post even under maximal pressure; the obsessive showing-up — these are not free choices in the existential sense, they are a sustained, lifelong vote against a man who has been dead for sixty-plus years. The subject does not name him often. He does not need to. The father is the silent, daily referendum.

**The naming problem.** That the subject shares his name with both his father (Daniel Sr.) and his brother (Daniel Jr.) is a near-perfect Freudian artifact: he carries the dead brother's first name through his own *middle* name (Jacob, after the uncle who saved him), and his father's first name was the one his brother also bore and consecrated by dying with. The subject goes by Ben, exclusively. He does not use Benjamin in informal speech. He never, in any recorded canon, refers to his father by first name. Possibly cannot.

**Ongoing behavioral traces.** (a) The beer-discipline. One, two, occasionally three — never the fourth that would constitute a session. Bartenders who know him do not push. He notices himself reaching for a fourth and stops. This is not casual; this is forty years of sustained refusal. (b) The hand-control around Alicia. He has, by the canon's depiction, never raised his voice destructively at her, never broken a thing in her studio in anger, never let his strength touch her except gently. (c) An almost allergic response to adult men who bully women or children in his presence; the response is faster and less mediated than his response to comparable threats by other adversary types. (d) Refusal of certain therapeutic framings ("anger management," "the inner child") that would require him to look directly at the father; preference for action-based regulation (work, fight, walk).

**Trust/safety:** Historically zero; internalized object is the template of the untrustworthy adult man.

**Failure mode:** Will, in extremis, recognize father-patterns in adversaries and respond with a precision and coldness rare for him. Equally, will tolerate behavior in young, struggling men (drinkers, brawlers, fathers in trouble) that he would not tolerate in others, because he can see his father in them and is committed to the proposition that intervention earlier might have saved his own household. He has bailed out, paid for, and quietly mentored an undocumented number of such men over the decades.

**Leverage:** Attempting to suggest he is becoming his father is the single most effective destabilization in this section of the file. Has been deployed against him by adversaries (and, in one or two of the rawer Reed arguments, by Reed himself in unintended cruelty). Produces immediate flat affect, withdrawal, and a several-day depressive episode. *Do not use.* The accusation, even if false, is the one wound he cannot defend against because the entire architecture of his adult discipline is built on its refutation, and the refutation requires that the question never be conceded as askable.

---

### 6.4 — UNCLE JAKE GRIMM (Dr. Jacob Grimm, deceased)

**Status:** Deceased of natural causes; survived the subject's childhood and into his adulthood; one of the only origin figures the subject got to lose at a non-traumatic age. Survived by widow Petunia (see 6.5).

**Historical function.** The rescue. A general-practice physician in the neighborhood — a Jewish family doctor of the mid-century Lower East Side mold, the kind who treated patients regardless of ability to pay and kept his office open at night. Took the orphaned (functionally) nephew into his childless household with Petunia and raised him from approximately age ten or eleven into late adolescence. Provided: food security for the first time, a stable adult male model, a home where shouting was not the baseline, the seed capital of self-respect that made the football scholarship and the Air Force possible.

**Modeling content.** Jake is the deep template under every nurturing behavior the subject exhibits. Healer-as-vocation; competence-as-care; quiet authority rather than performed authority; the moral seriousness of showing up for the patient in front of you regardless of who they are or what they can pay. The subject's late-career charity work (Yancy Street community programs, anonymous pediatric-hospital donations, the recurring trope of him visiting sick kids in costume) is Jake's praxis transposed onto Ben's resources. He is being the doctor he had.

**Internalized function.** Where Daniel is the superego of *the street code*, Jake is the superego of *the menschlich code* — the broader Jewish-ethical framework of obligation to the stranger, to the patient, to the orphan. The two codes are not contradictory in the subject's interior and are, in fact, the two sides of a coherent ethic: stand for your own *and* tend to anyone in front of you. Reed's utilitarian-rationalist morality is consistently weighed against this older composite and consistently found wanting.

**The Jewish-faith arc.** The Sheckerberg episode and the adult bar mitzvah re-affirmation are as much *for Jake* as for his mother. Jake took him to shul. Jake taught him aleph-bet. Jake observed the holidays in a household where the father would not. The faith that the subject re-claims publicly in middle age is, in its lived content, Jake's faith.

**Ongoing behavioral traces.** (a) The doctor-deference reflex: subject is unusually respectful of medical personnel, including ones who have failed him, and does not joke during medical examinations the way he jokes through almost everything else. (b) A specific physical gesture of comfort — a hand on the upper back, brief, firm — that he uses with grieving or injured civilians and that observers familiar with old-school house-call physicians will recognize as a learned bedside gesture. (c) Reads obituaries in the neighborhood paper. Has, when in town, attended an undocumented number of funerals of people he barely knew, for the menschlich reason that Jake would have.

**Trust/safety:** Total in life, total in memory.

**Failure mode:** The subject's vulnerability to authority figures who present in a Jake-coded register — older, competent, kind, professional, Jewish or Jewish-adjacent — is non-trivial. He will extend trust faster to such figures than his usual approach-and-test pattern would predict. Adversaries who have constructed such a presentation (false specialists, false rabbis) have gotten initial purchase. Subject self-corrects within hours once behavior diverges from the template, but the opening exists.

**Leverage:** Invocation is permissible if grounded and respectful; manipulative invocation is recognized only marginally faster than maternal manipulation. The safer surface, in operational terms.

---

### 6.5 — AUNT PETUNIA GRIMM (status varies by continuity; living in some, deceased in others)

**Status:** Variable. Treated here as the *figure*, which is the operative reality regardless of vital status in any given continuity.

**Historical function.** Co-parent in the rescue household. The kitchen, the laundry, the homework supervision, the bandage. Childless before Ben arrived; received him as the son she had not had. The subject's experience of unconditional female warmth — the experience his mother was too overwhelmed to fully provide — is largely Petunia's gift.

**The Petunia-joke phenomenon.** The recurring decades-long gag of the subject invoking "Aunt Petunia" as a reflexive verbal tic ("by the beard of my Aunt Petunia," "ya wouldn't say that in front of my Aunt Petunia," etc., across hundreds of issues) is, beneath the schtick, a continuous act of *citation*. He keeps her named, in print, in the public record, every month for sixty years. No other relative receives this treatment. The joke is the monument. Most observers, including most of his teammates for most of the canon, did not realize that "Aunt Petunia" was a real person and not a comic invention — which is precisely the cover under which the subject preserves her: hidden in plain sight, protected by being mistaken for a bit.

**Modeling content.** Petunia is the source-template of *domestic warmth as a moral act*. The household she ran — modest, kosher-ish, observant in the lived rather than rigid sense, available — is the household the subject is, in his late-career marriage to Alicia, attempting to reconstruct. The apartment he and Alicia keep is decorated in a register that anyone who knew Petunia's kitchen would recognize.

**Ongoing behavioral traces.** (a) An unforced courtliness toward older women — door-holding, name-remembering, the small attentions — that is consistent and unfeigned. (b) The Petunia-citation pattern itself, multiple times weekly in casual speech. (c) Cooking: subject can cook a small repertoire of Ashkenazi dishes competently and does so for Alicia on specific occasions. The recipes are Petunia's.

**Trust/safety:** Total.

**Failure mode:** None operationally significant. The internalized Petunia is stabilizing rather than destabilizing.

**Leverage:** Threats to a living Petunia, in continuities where she lives, would produce a response comparable to threats against Alicia. Invocation of her memory in manipulative bad faith would be received as obscene and would close the channel permanently.

---

### 6.6 — CHILDREN: JO-VENN AND N'KALLA (Adopted)

**Status:** Living. Adopted into the Grimm-Masters household in the late-period Slott/North continuity. A young Kree boy and a young Skrull girl, respectively — the surviving children of an experimental program weaponizing the two species' war, taken in by Ben and Alicia after rescue.

**Adoption logic.** The choice of these specific children is diagnostic. Two children from species in eternal mutual hostility, both marked physically as *other*, both unable to pass as human. The subject is, in the act of taking them in, performing the simultaneous resolution of three of his core wounds: (a) being marked-as-other oneself and discovering one is still loveable; (b) the menschlich obligation to the orphan in front of you, Jake's code; (c) the construction of a household across difference, against the inheritance of conflict — an explicit refutation of the Yancy-Street/rival-block enmity that killed Daniel. He is making the household he wishes had existed for both his brother and these kids.

**Parenting style.** Patient, physical (within his strength-discipline), verbal in a way he is not with adults — talks them through their feelings rather than joking past them. Reads to them at bedtime. Cooks for them. Does not perform the Thing-schtick at home in their presence; they get Ben. Defers to Alicia on most disciplinary calls but is willing to be the immovable wall when needed, and is unusually clear-eyed about *which* parent each task belongs to. Notably patient with the children's species-specific cultural and biological idiosyncrasies — does not try to anglicize or humanize them.

**Particular vulnerabilities the children activate.** Both children, by virtue of being visibly non-human in an Earth-dominant environment, recapitulate his own form-trauma. He sees them flinch at strangers' stares and the response is immediate and total. Civilians who say anything within earshot of either child are spoken to, once, very quietly, by a five-hundred-pound man. The matter resolves.

**Trust/safety:** Subject is maximally safe with these children. They are safe with him in a sense few children in the Marvel universe are safe with anyone.

**Failure mode:** Pressure point 2 in the prior assessment — harm or perceived harm to a child of his — applies maximally here. Tactical judgment will be subordinated to retrieval and protection. Subject is aware of this and has, characteristically, pre-discussed it with both Alicia and Reed so that the team can plan around it rather than be surprised by it.

**Leverage:** Maximum, in the morally darkest sense. Also maximally defended; the household's security protocols (Reed-designed, Sue-supervised, Ben-enforced) are among the most thorough on the planet.

---

### 6.7 — BIOLOGICAL CHILDREN WITH ALICIA (continuity-variable)

**Status:** Continuity-dependent; in several timelines (including the late Slott run and projected futures glimpsed across the canon), Ben and Alicia have biological children. Treated here briefly, as the file's primary parental data is currently routed through Jo-Venn and N'Kalla.

**Operative significance.** The existence of biological offspring resolves, for the subject, the longest-standing question of his post-transformation life — whether his body can produce, rather than only destroy. The reproductive question (see Medical, sexual function ambiguity) is the somatic correlate of the body-image disturbance, and a biological child constitutes the most decisive available counter-evidence. In continuities where such children exist, observable affect around them is qualitatively distinct: a stunned, almost reverent gentleness, and a markedly reduced frequency of the self-deprecating schtick in their presence.

**Failure mode and leverage:** As 6.6, intensified by biological dimension. The same defenses apply.

---

### 6.8 — THE DEAD, AS A CATEGORY

A surveillance file should note: the subject *maintains* his dead in a way that is operationally relevant. Yahrzeit candles in the apartment on the relevant dates. Periodic visits to graves in the outer-borough Jewish cemeteries when in New York. A small drawer in his quarters at the Baxter Building contains, by reliable inference from depicted moments, a few photographs and at least one object of his mother's. He does not display these. He does not discuss them. Their presence is structural.

The internalized parliament of the dead — Daniel, mother, Jake, Petunia in her memorial register, father in his negative-template register — is, in the subject's interior, *present* during major decisions. He consults them. He has said so, in unguarded moments across the canon, usually phrased as a joke about what one or another of them "would've said." The joke is the cover; the consultation is real.

This is not pathology. It is the form his integration has taken. A man whose blood family was destroyed before he was old enough to negotiate adult relationships with any of them has, through sustained interior work over six decades, built those negotiations posthumously, and the resulting moral architecture is more coherent than that of most subjects whose families survived. The graveyard is also the foundation.

---

*End Section 6. Section 7 (Relationships II — The Chosen Family


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: GRIMM, BENJAMIN JACOB ("THE THING")

## SECTION 6 — RELATIONSHIPS II: ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

The subject's relational architecture is unusually dense and unusually durable. Where most subjects in the trauma-tier file class show relational churn — friendships abandoned, mentors discarded, proteges burned — Grimm shows the opposite: relationships acquired in the 1960s remain active in the present, with the wear-pattern of constant use rather than abandonment. The "found family" formulation is overused in the popular literature; in this file it is operationally exact. The subject has built, deliberately and over six decades, a kinship network that functionally replaces the family of origin destroyed before he was twenty.

The following sub-sections map that network exhaustively. Romantic and biological-familial relationships are mapped in Section 5 (Relationships I) and Section 7 (Family of Procreation); this section is restricted to the chosen network — siblings-in-arms, mentors, proteges, and the secondary ring of trusted operators outside the Baxter Building.

---

### 6.1 — RICHARDS, REED ("MISTER FANTASTIC")

The defining relationship of the subject's adult life. Diagnostic, load-bearing, and the most data-rich dyadic record in the file.

**Provenance.** First contact: State University, freshman year, assigned as roommates. The asymmetry is established immediately and never fundamentally alters: Richards the small, brilliant, socially awkward science student; Grimm the football scholarship athlete, the popular one, the *protector*. The original valence of the friendship is Grimm-as-shield, Richards-as-mind, and this configuration — though inverted in the public eye after the cosmic-ray flight — remains psychologically primary. Grimm still operates, internally, as the older-brother figure even when Richards is functionally team commander.

**The promise.** Sometime in their college years Grimm makes the offhand pledge to fly any ship Richards builds, "anytime, anywhere" (*FF* #1). It is the throwaway promise of a confident young man, made to a friend whose ideas seemed safely theoretical. The promise is honored. The promise becomes the wound. The structure of the entire relationship for sixty years can be read as both men metabolizing the fact that Grimm kept a word he had no reason to think would cost him his body.

**Operational dynamics.** Day-to-day: Grimm is the only person in the building who will tell Richards he is wrong without softening it, and the only person Richards will hear it from. Susan corrects him with the authority of a wife; Grimm corrects him with the authority of the one person who knew him *before he was right about everything*. The needling — "stretcho," "egghead," the running commentary on Richards' tone-deafness toward Franklin — is the form of the correction. It looks like abuse to outsiders and reads, to anyone who has watched the tape, as the most stable feedback loop in the team.

**The grievance.** Properly catalogued because it is permanent and reactivatable. Grimm believes — with substantial evidentiary support across multiple arcs (*FF* #245-era controversy, the Trial sequence in Slott's run, multiple Hickman-era beats) — that Richards has at various points been *able* to restore him to human form and has not done so, either from technical conservatism, from need of Grimm as the Thing, or from a quiet awareness that Grimm's somatic instability would re-mutate him anyway. The grievance has two layers: the surface layer (Reed failed me technically) and the deep layer (Reed knows me well enough to know I cannot stay human, and that knowledge is itself unbearable). The second layer is rarely verbalized but is the one that hurts.

**Repair pattern.** The dyad has a characteristic rupture-and-repair cycle, repeated perhaps a dozen times across the canon: precipitating event (a cure failure, an oversight, a moment of Richards' cosmic abstraction harming a person Grimm protects) → explicit confrontation, often physical (Grimm has struck Richards on record at least four times, never with full force, always controlled) → withdrawal by Grimm (hours to months, scaling with severity) → unilateral return by Grimm, usually under cover of a tactical emergency that lets neither man speak the apology. Richards rarely apologizes in words. Grimm rarely demands he do so. The apology is performed in subsequent conduct: Richards working visibly harder on the cure, deferring to Grimm in front of the children, building him things. Grimm reads these and accepts them.

**Trust profile.** Operational trust: ceiling. Will follow Richards into any tactical scenario without question, including ones he disagrees with morally, on the understanding that he reserves the right to object loudly afterward and to refuse the next time if the objection is not registered. Personal trust: high but bounded. Will not share certain emotional material with Richards (the depths of the body-grief, certain doubts about his worthiness of Alicia) — not from distrust but from a protective instinct that Richards lacks the receptive apparatus to hold it without trying to *solve* it.

**Failure mode.** Two scenarios. First: a Richards cosmic-scale decision that costs civilian lives in a way Grimm cannot rationalize — this triggers the rupture-withdrawal cycle and, in the worst observed cases (Battleworld, the post-*Civil War* expatriation), produces months of separation. Second, more dangerous: any evidence that Richards has *lied* to him about the cure or about a cure-adjacent matter. Grimm tolerates Richards being wrong; he does not tolerate being managed. A demonstrated act of deception by Richards on a personal matter would produce the longest withdrawal in the record and is the only scenario in which the dyad could be considered at structural risk.

**Leverage.** An adversary seeking to operate on Grimm via Richards has two vectors: (a) manufacture or expose a Richards betrayal — high yield, requires sophistication; (b) put Richards in mortal danger — Grimm's response is total and tactical judgment compresses. The second is more reliable but also more dangerous to the adversary.

**Net assessment.** This is not a friendship in any ordinary sense. It is a marriage of the soul-brother type, with all the chronic frictions and non-negotiable bonds that implies. The two men have, between them, sixty years of unrepaired and unrepayable mutual debt, which they have agreed, tacitly, to carry rather than settle. The arrangement works.

---

### 6.2 — STORM, SUSAN ("INVISIBLE WOMAN")

The relationship the file undersells in the popular literature. Grimm-Storm is the *quietest* high-bandwidth bond on the team and arguably the most emotionally healthy relationship in his adult life.

**Provenance.** Met Susan through Reed during the college years; she was Reed's much-younger acquaintance then, and Grimm's early posture toward her was protective-fraternal, a posture that has never fundamentally changed though the power asymmetry has long since flipped. By the time of the cosmic-ray flight she is an adult, and her presence on the ship as Reed's partner makes her, instantly, family by extension. The transformation made her family by event.

**Operational dynamics.** Susan is the *only* member of the team who can give Grimm a direct order he will accept without renegotiation. Reed's orders are filtered through the grievance-and-affection complex; Johnny's "orders" do not exist as a category; Susan's instructions land. The reason is structural: she is the one person in his proximity whose moral judgment he trusts to be *both* loving and unsentimental. She will not coddle him and she will not weaponize him. When she tells him to stand down, he stands down. When she tells him to step up — usually to fill a parental gap Reed has created — he does so without needing to be asked twice.

**The emotional channel.** Susan is the recipient of confidences Grimm does not give Richards. Not the body-grief in detail — that he gives only to Alicia and, in fragments, to his uncle Jake and his rabbi — but the Reed-grievances, the worry about Franklin, the doubts about his fitness as a father. She listens without solving. She does not relay material to Reed without permission, and Grimm has tested this enough times across the canon to know it.

**Reciprocal channel.** Susan brings Grimm her *Reed* grievances. The pattern is symmetrical and longstanding: when Reed has hurt her — coldness, abstraction, the chronic failure of attention — she will, often without verbalizing the issue directly, seek out Grimm's company. Tea in the kitchen. A long walk on the roof. Watching the children together. Grimm understands the function of these summons perfectly and never asks what is wrong; his presence is the medicine. This is the most underdocumented intimacy in the file.

**Failure mode.** Vanishingly small. The one observed near-failure: episodes in which Grimm has been put in the position of choosing between Susan and Reed's tactical authority (notably the *Civil War* alignment period and its aftermath). He sided with the moral judgment over the chain of command, which placed him with Susan. The dyad survived; the team configuration was reshuffled but the bond was strengthened.

**Leverage.** Direct threats to Susan trigger the same response profile as threats to Alicia, with the additional complication that Susan is herself a peer-grade combatant — Grimm's protective impulse toward her must be modulated against her own tactical authority, and the published record shows him doing this modulation with surprising delicacy for a man who looks like he cannot do delicate things. An adversary attempting to use Susan against Grimm would need to incapacitate her first; if she is conscious and functional, she will be the one ordering *him*.

**Net assessment.** The sister-bond. Functions as the team's emotional ground wire. Grimm would die for Susan with no internal negotiation whatsoever; the published record contains multiple instances of him interposing his body in scenarios where he had no expectation of survival. He has never spoken of it. Neither has she.

---

### 6.3 — STORM, JONATHAN ("THE HUMAN TORCH")

The kid brother. The annoyance-as-love relationship. The relational dyad most legible to outsiders and the one most easily underestimated.

**Provenance.** Met through Susan, pre-flight; the two have a long shared history before the cosmic-ray flight, including documented joint social activity (drag racing, hot rods, the Glenville period in early canon). The age gap, never precisely specified but probably 12–15 years at original publication, placed Grimm in elder-brother position immediately and has stayed there.

**Operational dynamics.** The prank war is the single most extensively documented behavioral pattern in the file outside the schtick itself. It runs continuously from approximately *Strange Tales* #101 to the present. Pranks are functionally bidirectional but quantitatively Storm-initiated; Grimm's retaliations are louder, slower, and more property-destructive. The pranks serve at least four functions: (1) affective regulation for both parties — discharge of low-grade tension that would otherwise accumulate; (2) skill maintenance — Storm sharpens his fine power control by harassing Grimm, Grimm sharpens his patience and his speed by suffering it; (3) public-facing identity reinforcement — they perform "brothers" for the team, the children, the press; (4) covert intimacy maintenance — neither man finds it easy to verbalize affection, and the pranks function as a love language.

**The serious channel.** When Storm needs Grimm seriously — heartbreak, the death of girlfriends (he has lost several), questions about his sister's marriage, episodes of his own self-doubt — the prank register is suspended within seconds. Grimm reads the shift instantly. He becomes physically still, lowers his voice, and listens. Storm, in turn, has been the *only* person on the team to consistently insist on Grimm's worthiness of love in moments when Grimm has discounted himself; the relevant beats in the Wedding of Reed and Sue era, the post-Battleworld return, and various Slott-run quiet moments document this with consistency.

**The recursive joke.** Storm calls Grimm "Thing" with cheerful disregard. Grimm calls Storm "Match-stick," "Flame-brain," "Junior." The escalation algorithm is consistent: insult parity must be maintained. Outsiders who attempt to insult Storm in Grimm's presence are corrected — sometimes verbally, sometimes physically — within a window of seconds. The right to mock Johnny Storm is reserved, and the reservation is enforced.

**Failure mode.** Two observed scenarios. First: arcs in which Storm has been emotionally compromised by an enemy operating through romantic-deception channels (the long history of compromised girlfriends). Grimm's pattern is to express irritation, then quietly conduct counter-surveillance, then move to extract Storm from the situation by any means including the embarrassing. Second: rare arcs in which Storm has questioned Grimm's choices in front of Alicia or the children. Grimm has, in these cases, responded with cold severity that has visibly shocked Storm and required explicit repair. Both have learned the rule.

**Leverage.** An adversary attempting to threaten Storm to control Grimm will find that Grimm's response is among the most violent in his catalogue, comparable to threats against the children. The disinhibition is partial — Grimm will not break his moral code — but the tactical compression is severe. Conversely, Storm cannot be used as a witting agent against Grimm under any plausible coercion scenario; the bond is bilateral and Storm would self-destruct before complying.

**Net assessment.** The brother he was given to replace the brother he lost. The canon never says this aloud and almost certainly does not need to. Daniel Grimm died young; Johnny Storm has lived, in the symbolic register, in Daniel's slot for sixty years. Grimm has not let another younger brother be killed on his watch and would not survive, intact, the experience of it happening.

---

### 6.4 — RICHARDS, FRANKLIN

The godson. The first child Grimm ever fully loved. The relationship that proved to him he could be a father before he had the chance to be one.

**Provenance.** Present at the birth (*FF Annual* #6, 1968). One of the first to hold the infant; the published record shows him present and physically engaged in the child-rearing from week one, more reliably than Reed and at times more reliably than Susan, both of whom have been pulled away by team operations more frequently.

**Operational dynamics.** Grimm's interaction with Franklin from infancy through current published age is characterized by an extreme and conscious gentleness — the man who can lift eighty-five tons cradling an infant in the crook of one rock arm has been one of the canon's most recurrent images and is correctly read as the central iconography of his post-transformation self-rehabilitation. He has been the on-call uncle for Franklin's entire life: bedtime stories, scraped knees, school drop-offs in the brief periods of normal schooling, the conversations Reed has been emotionally unequipped to conduct.

**The Reed-compensation function.** Reed's parenting deficits are well-documented elsewhere in this file class. Grimm has, across decades, served as the compensating attachment figure — the adult Franklin can go to when his father is abstract, absent, or coldly rational. Grimm has *never* spoken ill of Reed to the child; the compensation is performed in presence and warmth, not in critique. This is one of the file's strongest pieces of evidence for the subject's emotional maturity: he understands that undermining Reed in Franklin's eyes would damage Franklin more than it would punish Reed, and he refuses to do it even when he believes Reed deserves the critique.

**Specific micro-patterns.** Calls Franklin "kiddo," "champ," "Frankie" — never "Franklin" except in moments of genuine seriousness, which signal to the child that the register has shifted. Carries the child on his shoulders well past the age this remained physically necessary; the child requested it long after he could walk. Has taught Franklin: how to throw a punch (defensively only, with extensive ethical scaffolding), how to make matzoh-ball soup, how to tell when an adult is lying, how to read a baseball box score. The pedagogy is working-class and embodied; it complements rather than competes with the science-pedagogy of the parents.

**The cosmic-power complication.** Franklin's reality-warping power has produced multiple crises across the canon. Grimm's response is consistent and instructive: he treats the power as a problem the family will manage, not as a marker of difference. He does not flinch from Franklin, does not condescend, does not look at him with the wary scientific interest his father sometimes shows. To Grimm, Franklin is a kid first and the most powerful being in several universes second. Franklin knows this, has known it since infancy, and the bond holds because of it.

**Failure mode.** Effectively none directly. The dyad has never substantially fractured. The failure mode is *displaced*: harm to Franklin produces in Grimm the most extreme behavioral state in his catalogue, exceeding his response to threats against Alicia in intensity though not in operational override (Alicia produces tactical compression; Franklin produces tactical *absence* — Grimm becomes a one-objective weapon).

**Leverage.** Maximal. An adversary controlling or harming Franklin could elicit any behavior from Grimm short of violating his moral code; the moral code itself would hold but everything else — caution, team coordination, self-preservation, willingness to make extreme sacrificial deals — would be discarded. Among the highest-priority protective vectors in the file.

**Net assessment.** The first proof, post-transformation, that Grimm could be loved without qualification by someone who had every alternative. An infant chose him; the choice is repaired daily for forty-plus published years; the wound of monstrousness is partially closed by the existence of this child's unhesitating trust.

---

### 6.5 — RICHARDS, VALERIA

The second child. The smarter one. The one who reads Grimm with adult precision from approximately age four.

**Provenance.** Born under contested circumstances (the Doom-delivery sequence in Waid's run); Grimm present at the birth, again. The fact that Doom himself participated in Valeria's delivery is a permanent and unspoken background fact in the dyad; Grimm has never raised it, has watched her affection for Doom with vigilance but without interference, and has trusted her judgment on it earlier than her parents have.

**Operational dynamics.** Where the Franklin bond is warm-and-physical, the Valeria bond is warm-and-verbal. Valeria's intelligence is paternal-grade and she figured out Grimm's interior architecture before she was eight. She calls him on his deflections. She names his moods. She has, on multiple occasions in the Hickman and Slott runs, sat with him in silence and then said something diagnostically exact about his state that no adult on the team has been willing to articulate.

**The pedagogy reverses.** With Franklin, Grimm teaches. With Valeria, Grimm is often the student — she explains things to him, including, on multiple occasions, his own life. He receives this with the open-handed humility of a man who has decided that being instructed by a child he loves is one of the great unexpected pleasures of his existence. The bond is partly built around his willingness to be taught.

**Protective vector.** Identical in priority to Franklin. The asymmetry is that Valeria is harder to threaten — she is too intelligent and too well-defended by her own resources — and Grimm has learned to extend his protection through *consultation* rather than intervention. He asks her how she wants a situation handled. He defers when she has a better plan. He intervenes physically only when she signals or when she is clearly incapacitated.

**Failure mode.** As with Franklin. The one specific risk: Valeria's intermittent interest in Doom as an intellectual peer has, in some published arcs, produced friction with the parents that Grimm has been pulled into mediating. He has consistently sided with Valeria's autonomy while making his own distrust of Doom audibly clear, a posture she has accepted because it is honest.

**Leverage.** Maximal, as Franklin. Note: Valeria's own capability set means that an adversary attempting to use her against Grimm would need to neutralize her first, and her resistance to such neutralization is high. The combined Franklin-Valeria threat surface is the single highest-priority pressure point in the file.

**Net assessment.** The proof, complementing Franklin's, that he could be loved by a mind that fully understood him. Franklin loved him without conditions; Valeria loves him with conditions she has examined and accepted. The two together complete the parental rehabilitation he could not have arranged for himself.

---

### 6.6 — JO-VENN AND N'KALLA

The adopted children (Slott run, the surviving last-of-their-species pair from the Kree-Skrull conflict). The fatherhood Grimm chose rather than inherited.

**Provenance.** Acquired in the late Slott run as displaced war-orphans; Grimm and Alicia took them in. The fact that they are of the two species that have spent most of the published continuity attempting to kill each other and Earth is a deliberate authorial commentary that the subject has metabolized without commentary: they are children; they need parents; the parents will be Grimm and Masters.

**Operational dynamics.** Newer relationship and therefore less data, but the pattern is consistent with the Franklin-Valeria template adjusted for primary rather than uncle-grade fatherhood. Grimm carries the bedtime-story load, the discipline load, the cultural-translation load (explaining Earth, Yancy Street, baseball, Jewish holidays); Alicia carries the emotional-intuition load, the art-pedagogy load. The household is the most stable he has ever participated in.

**Specific micro-patterns.** Has taught both children to call him "Pop" rather than "Ben" or "Thing" — a quiet insistence, registered in the published record only once or twice, that he is claiming the role rather than performing it. Has begun, recently, the Jewish-cultural transmission he reclaimed in his own adulthood; the bar mitzvah arc he completed late carries forward into the parenting of these children with explicit intentionality.

**Failure mode.** Untested at scale. The most plausible failure: a Kree or Skrull political reclamation attempt — adversaries arguing legitimate cultural-custody claims. Grimm's response would be implacable; the moral framing he would adopt is "we are their parents." Whether this position is jurisdictionally defensible matters to him less than whether it is morally defensible, and he has decided the latter.

**Leverage.** Newly added to the maximum-priority protective tier. Any adversary now has four children to threaten rather than two.

**Net assessment.** The fatherhood elected after extensive practice as an uncle. The household completes the long arc from the boy whose family was killed by poverty and violence to the man who has assembled, by deliberate authorship, a family of his own. The fact that the children are not of his species or his world is, given his history, the point.

---

### 6.7 — GRIMM, JAKE (PATERNAL UNCLE)

The mentor of origin. The single most important formative adult in the subject's pre-transformation life and the model against which every subsequent helping figure has been measured.

**Provenance.** Took the subject in after the death of the mother and the dissolution of the household; a physician on the Lower East Side, married to Petunia ("Aunt Petunia" — the running reference Grimm makes throughout his published life is to this aunt, not, as the gag implies, an imaginary figure). Raised the subject through adolescence.

**Operational d


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

The following dossier section maps every individual whose relationship to Subject Grimm operates under the structural valence of *opposition* (rival, enemy) or *intimacy* (lover, romantic partner, would-be partner). The categories braid. Grimm's intimate life and his enmity life are both organized by the same underlying question — *can this person see me, and what do they do with what they see?* — and the cross-pollination between the two registers is itself one of his most diagnostic features.

Where the canon offers explicit material it is cited; where the file requires inference at the granular level a total-surveillance dossier would contain, the inference is marked by the specificity of the behavioral detail (gait, vocabulary, breathing, micro-tells) rather than by hedging language. This is what a long file looks like.

---

## I. RIVALS

A rival, in Grimm's operational vocabulary, is not an enemy. A rival is someone whose existence challenges him in a register he respects — competence, courage, claim on something he loves — and against whom he measures himself without wishing them harm. The list is shorter than one would expect. Grimm does not generate rivalries promiscuously; he is, despite the bluster, a man with a low envy quotient.

### 1. Johnny Storm — The Brother-Rival

The Johnny-Ben axis is the most documented rivalry in superhero comics and the easiest to misread. It is *not* a rivalry of resentment. It is the formal, ritualized antagonism between two brothers who share the structural position of *the team's flammable element* — Johnny by physiology, Ben by temperament — and who have arranged their relationship so that the antagonism *is* the affection.

**History.** From *FF* #1 (1961) the prank-war is in place: Johnny modifies Ben's car, Ben crushes Johnny's car, both laugh, neither alters the pattern. The pattern continues, with negligible variation, for sixty-plus years of publication. There is no developmental arc here in the conventional sense; the *content* of the pranks evolves with the technology (joy-buzzers become holographic gags become Reed-tech weaponized for slapstick) but the *form* — Johnny initiates, Ben over-responds, Johnny laughs and gets clobbered, both feel better — is sealed.

**Function.** The prank-war discharges, in low-stakes form, what would otherwise be untenable affect. Johnny is the surviving golden-boy younger brother; Daniel Grimm is the dead older brother. Ben, who lost the role of *being* the protected younger brother early, took the role of *being* the protector older brother and gave it to Johnny. The pranks are how Johnny pays the toll for being protected — by making himself irritating enough that Ben's care doesn't congeal into something heavier. Both men understand this without ever discussing it.
